Current Commentary

The Chahar-Northern Negotiation, Worthy of Great Attention 14

— Ji

The successive incidents in Eastern Hebei and Northern Chahar are manifestations of a planned and step-by-step northward-offensive and southward-defensive policy directed by a certain party. The reporter has already made some comments on this matter (see the current commentary in this newspaper on December 27 of last year). Now, after a lapse of ten days, the development of the situation has exceeded expectations. After the pseudo-army of Li Shouxin occupied the six counties of Guyuan, Kangbao, Baochang, Shangdu, Zhangbei, and Wanquan in Northern Chahar, it even attempted to intrude into eastern Suiyuan. The remnants of the bandit Liu Guitang, entrenched in Yanching in the Chahar territory, also took the opportunity to flee westward. As a result, the five counties of Fengzhen, Jining, Taolin, and Helingcheng in eastern Suiyuan felt the threat of the western invasion of the Northern Chahar pseudo-army and were quite alarmed. Fu Zuoyi, Chairman of Suiyuan Province, had no choice but to actively increase defenses in eastern Suiyuan. As for the diplomatic aspect, in addition to the central government's submission of negotiations to the Japanese side, Song Zheyuan and others have also recently negotiated with Tanaka Ryuichi, staff officer of the Japanese Kwantung Army, and have made several decisions. Recently, it was heard that a principle of resolution was roughly agreed upon on the 5th of this month. The content is: The five counties of Zhangbei and others will be jointly defended by the provincial security team and the Mongolian banner security team. The administration will still be directly under the jurisdiction of the Chahar provincial government. The pseudo-army of Li Shouxin will all withdraw to Doron. According to the Japanese side, the reason for insisting that the Mongolian banner security team enter the counties of Zhangbei and others is to prevent communism. However, if this negotiation becomes an established fact, then although the Chahar provincial authorities still possess the nominal integrity of the territory, half of the Chahar province will in fact be reduced to a co-managed area. The impact will not only be a serious threat to the entire Suiyuan Province, but also to the provinces of Ningxia, Shaanxi, Xinjiang, and Shanxi. The severity of its nature cannot be ignored.

In recent years, the Japanese side's active westward work has been no less than its southward invasion. For example, the construction of the Doron airfield, the activities of the intelligence team, the anesthetization of Inner Mongolian youth, the training of the Mongolian banner security team, the seduction of Mongolian princes, and the coercion of local authorities are all worthy of deep attention. The Japanese side's intention is to use Doron as a center to control all of Chahar and Suiyuan, while simultaneously penetrating the northwestern provinces of China through the Chahar and Suiyuan provinces. When the Zhangbei dispute was being negotiated in July of last year, the Japanese side proposed demarcating the area of Doron, Guyuan, Dushikou, Chicheng, Yanching, and Huailai in eastern Chahar as a non-garrison area. This was a concrete manifestation of its active westward invasion, and it is regrettable that our side readily accepted it. Since then, the gateway of Chahar Province has been wide open, and the power of the invaders has been able to enter directly. This decision on the occurrence of the Northern Chahar incident is a consistent action. The so-called anti-communism is only a means to cover up its aggression.

Recently, the Northern Chahar negotiations have aroused the deep attention of foreigners, who believe that this is a major issue concerning the territorial integrity of China and the Russo-Japanese War. From the standpoint of the nation, we sincerely feel that the Northern Chahar incident is not a common local incident and must be dealt with carefully. Under this serious situation, what is hoped for from the North China authorities conducting the negotiations is: first, to carefully examine the relationship of interests and its future impact; second, to abandon nominal gains and value actual results and not delay and procrastinate due to the difficulty of the problem. Otherwise, the new situation that will arise after the Northern Chahar incident is resolved is not what we want to imagine.

Vice Chairman Chiang’s Report at the Memorial Week (Continued from Yesterday) 15

"The Great Path of Revolution and Nation-Building as a Person"

Every thought, every word, and every action of ours must be rooted in good intentions, originate from sincerity, be cautious in solitude, and never deviate from decisions made. We must know that all things in the world are born from this sincerity and sustained by it. If a single thought is insincere, then all things become false, and everything returns to nothingness. As the saying goes, "Sincerity is the beginning and end of things; without sincerity, there is nothing." We must deeply understand this profound principle and practice it with caution and reverence at all times. Only then can we achieve rectitude of mind and sincerity of intention, and complete the work of self-cultivation. The most important thing in the work of "sincerity of intention" is to "accept good and hold fast to it." Therefore, before we can be sincere in our intentions, we must be able to clearly distinguish between what is good and evil in all things. For example, we must first firmly recognize and believe that the Three Principles of the People are the only perfect and flawless revolutionary ideology for saving the country and the world. Only then can we go through fire and water, sacrificing everything to realize the ideology. Conversely, if we cannot clearly understand that the Three Principles of the People are the perfect and flawless revolutionary ideology, we cannot firmly believe and practice them, and we will be afraid of danger and sacrifice everywhere. Therefore, it is said, "Those who wish to be sincere in their intentions must first extend their knowledge." The Premier's teachings to us in general about revolutionary spirit, which are also the teachings for our general revolutionary party members, first emphasize "the wisdom of a soldier": first, "distinguish right from wrong"; second, "understand advantages and disadvantages"; third, "recognize the times"; and fourth, "know oneself and the enemy." In addition, the Premier also said that the foundation of revolution lies in profound knowledge. These precious posthumous teachings are meant to encourage us to strive for knowledge. We must extend our knowledge, and then we can sincerely and wholeheartedly carry out the ideology and complete the revolution. As for the method of "extending knowledge," the principle behind it is explained most clearly by Cheng Zi. He said, "The so-called extension of knowledge lies in the investigation of things, which means that to extend our knowledge, we must investigate things and exhaust their principles. For the human mind is inherently capable of knowing, and all things in the world have their principles. However, because the principles have not been exhausted, our knowledge is incomplete. Therefore, when the Great Learning begins its teachings, it must require students to investigate all things in the world, exhausting their principles based on the knowledge they already have, to seek the ultimate understanding. When they have exerted themselves for a long time, and suddenly one day they achieve a breakthrough and comprehensive understanding, then the external and internal, refined and coarse aspects of all things will be known, and the entirety and great function of our minds will be clear. This is called the investigation of things, and this is called the perfection of knowledge." When we read these words of his, we can understand that the so-called "extension of knowledge lies in the investigation of things" means "investigating things and exhausting their principles." For example, today, when I came to the Central Party Headquarters, I could see many things that need to be improved along the way. To be a revolutionary—that is, to be a statesman—and to govern the affairs of the people and the country well, the most important fundamental cultivation is to pay attention, observe, and study all things at all times and in all places, especially all social phenomena. Otherwise, you will not know the affairs of society and the country at all, let alone talk about governing society and the country well and completing the revolution. Therefore, "the investigation of things" is the beginning of all our cultivation and undertakings. "When things are investigated, knowledge is extended; when knowledge is extended, intentions are made sincere; when intentions are made sincere, the heart is rectified; when the heart is rectified, the person is cultivated; when a person is cultivated, the family is regulated; when the family is regulated, the state will be rightly governed; when the state is rightly governed, the whole world will be at peace." The above are the eight steps of the Great Learning, among which the most important is self-cultivation, because self-cultivation is at the center of the eight steps, serving as the pivot that connects the beginning and end, the internal and external, and the key to the intertwining of mind and matter, and the integration of virtue and achievement. It is also the foundation of all personal cultivation and undertakings. Therefore, Confucius said, "From the Son of Heaven down to the common people, all must regard self-cultivation as the root. It has never been the case that when the root is in disorder, the branches can be well governed." The so-called "Son of Heaven" used to refer to the emperor. Now, we should extend its meaning to refer to "leaders." A family has a head, an army has an officer, a group has a leader, and a country has a head of state. From the highest head of state to the people of the whole country, all must regard self-cultivation as the root. If one cannot cultivate oneself, one cannot only not carry out the revolutionary cause of regulating the family, governing the state, and bringing peace to the world, but also cannot be said to have achieved the goals of investigating things, extending knowledge, making intentions sincere, and rectifying the heart. Therefore, if one cannot cultivate oneself, one cannot only not do things, but also cannot be a person at all. The content of the Great Learning lies in the three guiding principles of "manifesting illustrious virtue," "renovating the people," and "resting in the highest excellence," and the eight steps of "investigating things, extending knowledge, making intentions sincere, rectifying the heart, cultivating the person, regulating the family, governing the state, and bringing peace to the world." If we want to be a person, we must know the principles of being a person, which are found here. If we want to make a revolution, govern the country, and bring peace to the world, we must know the principles of making a revolution, governing the country, and bringing peace to the world, which are also found here. This refined, comprehensive, and consistent principle is not only a unique treasure in our Chinese political philosophy, but also the basic scientific methodology for being a person and conducting business. Therefore, I say that the Great Learning is entirely scientific and entirely a scientific university. If we act according to the principles of the Great Learning, we can succeed in any undertaking. If we do not act according to the principles of the Great Learning, not only will all our efforts be in vain, but we will certainly end in failure. In the past, our comrades did not lack effort in the revolution, and they were very willing to sacrifice themselves. But why has the revolution not succeeded even after fifty years, and why has the country been brought to such a critical state of crisis? We must sincerely reflect on this reason and thoroughly awaken to it. Otherwise, the country will be lost, and we will not even know why. If we can all reflect and awaken, and make timely efforts, and from now on, everyone works together with one heart and one mind, acting according to the principles of the revolution, we will still have time to save the country, and the revolution can certainly be completed. When I was eighteen years old, I had read the Great Learning and the Doctrine of the Mean countless times, but I did not know the importance of the principles contained therein. I even thought that these antiquated things were completely useless because of the development of revolutionary thought. Later, when I was twenty-eight years old, I heard the Premier tell me the importance of the Great Learning and the Doctrine of the Mean, but I still did not pay much attention to it. It was not until I was thirty-eight years old, when my own experiences and knowledge had increased, that I took this book out again to study, and I realized that it was truly important. Almost all the principles for being a person and conducting business are contained therein. Since then, I have read it at least once a year, and the more I read it, the more I feel that there are infinite principles and endless mysteries within it. Now that I am forty-eight years old, on the one hand, I have been constantly studying it, and on the other hand, I have been constantly reflecting on the reasons for the past failures of the revolution and repenting that I did not complete the revolution earlier according to the principles of the Great Learning. I deeply feel that I have gained something in my heart that I can be confident in. Therefore, today, in the first Premier Memorial Week of the new year, I am presenting these thoughts to all comrades early on. If I did not say it, I would be letting down the Premier and all comrades, and letting down my own conscience. Now that I have said it, I hope that all comrades will act according to these inherent, proper, and unchangeable principles of China. Otherwise, the revolution will not succeed, and the country will be lost. At that time, we will not have time to regret it, and we will truly be letting down the Premier, letting down the 400 million compatriots of the country, and letting down our ancestors of the past 5,000 years. Therefore, from now on, all comrades in our party must encourage each other and lead by example, following the Premier's posthumous teachings and acting according to these revolutionary principles. Only then can we be models for the people, be worthy disciples of the Premier, and enable our party's life to be renewed day by day, and complete the mission of saving the country and the people. All the principles for being a person, making a revolution, governing the country, and bringing peace to the world are contained herein. I hope everyone will strive to put them into practice, and I wish you all a healthy New Year. (Central News Agency dispatch, 6th)

Recruiting Local Militias in Luan County; Villagers Prepare to Resist 16

Tianjin - The puppet Eastern Hebei government has reorganized the local militia of Luan County into the Eastern Hebei Army. The firearms carried by the militia were all purchased through public levies, worth more than 200,000 yuan. The people have lost their protection and suffered losses, and they are all complaining. The second phase of the Luan County militia is being recruited by Li Haitian, the commander of the puppet Third Security Brigade, and is divided into ten districts, with a quota of 1,000 men. The funds are levied on the local population, and the villages are brewing armed resistance. (Special dispatch, 7th)

Beiping - The Luan County militia was originally funded and organized by the people themselves. Now, it has been ordered to be reorganized into a formal army to garrison various places. All of the people's furniture and 4,000 firearms, as well as all other ammunition, have been taken away, worth a total of 200,000 yuan. The people have suffered heavy losses and are all complaining. After the Luan County militia was transferred away, bandits rose up. The county government decided in a meeting to organize a second phase of the militia this month and has ordered all districts in the county to start preparing through the security team and the county government. There are ten districts in the county, and a total of 1,000 militiamen will be recruited. (Special dispatch, 7th)

Tonight's Moon Can Be Seen Throughout the Country; There Will Be Two Solar and Two Lunar Eclipses This Year; Dispatching Personnel to Russia for Observation Is Still Undecided 19

Nanjing - According to the Central Observatory, there will be a total lunar eclipse after midnight on the 8th, which can be seen throughout the country. The initial eclipse will be at 0:28 on the 9th, the total eclipse will be at 1:58, the maximum eclipse will be at 2:10, the emergence will be at 2:21, and the eclipse will end at 3:51. In addition, there will be four eclipses this year, two solar and two lunar. In addition to the total lunar eclipse on the night of the 8th, there will also be a partial lunar eclipse on July 4th. The solar eclipses will be a total eclipse on June 19th and an annular eclipse on December 14th. The latter will not be visible in China. The former, except for the northwestern part of Heilongjiang Province, will only be visible as a partial eclipse. The path of the total solar eclipse will pass through the entire territory of Soviet Russia and Hokkaido, Japan. The governments of various countries have sent astronomers to participate in the observation. The Chinese Solar Eclipse Observation Committee, organized by academic circles in our country, has also decided to send personnel to participate, but due to a lack of funds, it is still unknown whether they will be able to make the trip. In addition, the most peculiar celestial phenomenon this year is the disappearance of Saturn's rings. We all know that Saturn has rings like the brim of a hat, but this year, the brim will not be visible twice, once at the end of June and once starting at the end of December, until February of next year. (Central News Agency dispatch, 7th)

A Car Accident in Qingzhen; Car Overturns into River in Gaoyou; Eight Bodies Have Been Recovered 20

Huaiyin - According to a telephone call from Gaoyou on the evening of the 6th, the second car heading south from Qingzhen arrived at Qigongdian in that county at noon. Due to carelessness while turning, it plunged into the river. There were 25 people on board, including the driver. By the evening, eight bodies had been recovered, four in military uniform and four in civilian clothes. The search for the remaining bodies is still underway. As soon as the news spread, the families of the passengers gathered at the telephone bureau to inquire, and they did not rest until midnight. This morning, many people went to the scene of the accident to investigate or prepare to move the bodies. (Special dispatch, 7th)

Huaiyin - Regarding the Qingzhen car accident, according to an employee of the company named Ping, a total of eight people drowned and more than ten were injured. The driver, Fu Xinfa, was seriously injured and is currently being held at the Gaoyou Public Security Bureau. The mechanic, Jin Guide, was also seriously injured. The accident was caused by the car overturning off the embankment. Tao Tianxing, the director of the Qing Bureau, took a special car to Gaoyou on the morning of the 7th to handle the aftermath. (Special dispatch, 7th)

Judicial Yuan Interprets Legal Doubts 27

Nanjing - The Judicial Yuan's interpretation of the doubts regarding the appeal against administrative sanctions misused by the county government兼理judicial in civil litigation cases is as follows: If the county government兼理judicial makes a judgment on a civil litigation case and misuses administrative sanctions, and the two parties express their dissatisfaction with the sanction, the higher court can correct it according to law. Furthermore, the Court of Further Appeal's legal judgment on the incident naturally has the effect of binding the original court. The Judicial Yuan's interpretation of the doubts regarding the district chief being accused of summoning the case is as follows: If a public official is accused and is deemed to be suspected of a crime, he may be summoned for questioning regardless of whether he has been suspended from duty or not. Tang Xiang, the original director of the Shandong-Henan Unified Tax Bureau, was transferred to serve as the superintendent of the Jinling Customs; Jia Guilin, the original superintendent of the Jinling Customs, was transferred to serve as the director of the Hebei Stamp and Tobacco Tax Bureau. Zeng Yangfeng, the original Salt Transport Commissioner of Changlu, was transferred to the ministry to await assignment. (Central News Agency dispatch, 7th)

"Soviet Foreign Policy": Collection of Litvinov's Speeches to Be Published 48

Moscow dispatch - The Soviet State Socio-Economic Literature Publishing House will publish a collection of Litvinov's speeches in January of next year, entitled "Soviet Foreign Policy." The book collects Litvinov's important speeches and declarations from 1927 to 1935, providing rich and valuable material on the evolution of international relations and the methods taken by Soviet foreign policy. The book includes the following chapters: Principles of Soviet Foreign Policy, The Soviet Union's Struggle for Disarmament, World Economy and the Soviet Union, The Soviet Union's Relations with Various Countries, and The Soviet Union's Struggle to Establish Collective Security, etc. (TASS, December 12)

Resumption of the Naval Conference: Differing Opinions Among Nations Persist, No Result on Notification of Shipbuilding Quantities, Hope for Qualitative Restrictions Diminished 49

London - Today, the naval conference resumed after a recess. Foreign Secretary Eden was elected as chairman, replacing former Foreign Secretary Hoare. Members continued to discuss the UK's proposal for each nation to unilaterally declare the number of warships they plan to build within a certain number of years. The Japanese representative criticized this proposal, stating that it was tantamount to maintaining a proportional system and would not reduce armaments. The British chief representative, First Lord of the Admiralty Monsell, replied that the idea of proportionality need not be overemphasized, and that the British plan could achieve reductions based on qualitative guidelines. The French chief representative, Roubier, put forward a new proposal, advocating that all signatory countries, including Germany, should report the types and armaments of all warships they plan to build to the League of Nations for dissemination to all countries six months in advance. He also advocated reducing the size of battleships and cruisers. The Italian delegation's spokesman put forward a similar proposal to Roubier's, advocating reporting shipbuilding programs annually as a general procedure, rather than the actual construction emphasized in the French plan. The US chief representative, Davis, spoke next, offering a general critique of the British, French, and Italian proposals. When the French representative Roubier mentioned that some countries might advocate a six-year period, Davis stated that any decided timeframe must be universally applied to all countries. He also stated that the work of the previous month's meeting was to consolidate the three proposals into one, or to select one of the three as a mechanism for seeking qualitative restrictions. The meeting was then adjourned to Wednesday to allow representatives to discuss the details of each proposal. Judging from the situation at today's meeting, the hope of reaching a qualitative restriction agreement has virtually disappeared. (Reuters, 6th)

London - After a sixteen-day recess, the naval conference resumed this afternoon. Before the recess, the UK had put forward a plan for quantitative restrictions (advocating that naval powers notify each other of their shipbuilding programs within a certain number of years, roughly set at six years). This proposal has failed. This is the most noteworthy event of today's meeting. France proposed that naval powers notify each other of their shipbuilding programs within a shorter period, which has been accepted by the UK for discussion. It is generally believed that the UK's purpose is to prolong the discussion of quantitative restrictions so that the naval conference does not completely fail due to Japan's opposition to the British plan. (Havas, 6th)

French Representative's New Proposal: Advocates Annual Notification of Shipbuilding Plans 50

London - The First Committee of the Disarmament Conference held its first meeting of the year at Clarence House at 3:16 PM. The Japanese delegation, including plenipotentiaries Nagano and Nagai, Rear Admiral Iwashita, Captain Inagaki, secretaries Fukumoto, Yamagata, and Terasaki, and official Inoue, attended. The US was represented by plenipotentiary Davis and Secretary Stanley. The UK was represented by First Lord of the Admiralty Monsell and Secretary Chatterfee, Councilor Craigie, etc. After Monsell announced the opening of the meeting, he proposed electing new Foreign Secretary Eden as chairman of the conference, which was unanimously approved. Next, discussion began on the British government's proposed shipbuilding declaration. French representative Vice Admiral Roubier spoke first, stating that pre-determining a long-term six-year shipbuilding plan would not be able to cope with changes in the international situation, and that the French government absolutely could not agree to a shipbuilding plan based on the current ratio. Therefore, the French representative presented the French government's shipbuilding notification proposal, the content of which is roughly as follows:

The signatory governments shall annually report their shipbuilding plans to all countries of the League of Nations.

Shipbuilding plans shall be decided independently by each government.

The participation of the German government in this notification proposal is a necessary condition. The French representative also mentioned qualitative restrictions and advocated reducing the size of battleships and cruisers. The US representative did not present any specific proposals. (Domei, 6th)

London - The General Committee of the Naval Conference continued its meeting at Clarence House this afternoon. Prior to the meeting, a certain French representative, at the urging of the UK, visited Fujii, an expert of the Japanese delegation, to inquire about Japan's attitude towards the British proposal. It was determined that Japan's opposition was firm and irreversible. According to recent news, the Japanese delegation had received instructions from the government during the recess to reject the British plan and any other proposals that did not grant Japan equal rights. After the General Committee meeting began, the British representative spoke first, defending his country's proposal. After a short debate, he accepted the French proposal for discussion. The French representative then explained his country's proposal, stating that a long-term quantitative restriction agreement was no longer possible because it would require establishing a permanent ratio of naval power for each country. Therefore, the naval conference should now seek to establish an agreement in which naval powers exchange information on their shipbuilding programs within a short period of time to understand each other's intentions. Since the financial capabilities of each country are different, this approach is actually sufficient to achieve the goal of restriction. Moreover, since the timeframe is short, each country can make modifications as needed to adapt to changes in the international situation. This is the advantage of the French proposal, he said. The Italian representative advocated a one-year limit for the exchange of shipbuilding information, as the budgets of each country are also based on one-year periods. The US representative said that the French proposal was worthy of consideration, but the Japanese representative adopted a wait-and-see attitude. The General Committee then adjourned. Tomorrow, France, the UK, and Italy will submit concrete proposals based on various data for each delegation to study, so that they can be submitted for discussion at the General Committee meeting on Wednesday. It is generally believed that if the French proposal is adopted, the shipbuilding programs of each naval power will be subject to the limitations of their national budget capabilities, and Japan will definitely express strong opposition. (Havas, 6th)

Tokyo - In order to cope with the breakdown of the Naval Conference, British Foreign Secretary Eden plans to divert the situation with a British-Japanese agreement on China. This has been reported repeatedly by two or three foreign dispatches. Japanese foreign affairs authorities attach great importance to this news, because the formal meeting to be continued is still in progress, and the appearance of the word "breakdown" is a cause for great concern. No matter what happens at the Naval Conference, it is limited to discussing naval disarmament issues. If political issues are added, it will be rejected, as this is the fundamental policy that has always been adhered to. Therefore, the following views are expressed:

Since the preliminary naval conference, the British government has hoped to conclude a British-Japanese agreement on China, solely for the purpose of ensuring British interests in China. However, the Japanese government has decided to avoid delving into this issue because the agenda of the naval conference has long been limited. In particular, the Japanese side believes that the true intention of the British government to limit the British-Japanese agreement to China is not its intention. The area most desired for agreement in British-Japanese commerce and trade is not China, but British territories outside of China. (Domei News Agency, 7th)

Economic Review 55

— Edited by Tang Qingzeng

Living Standards and Living Expenses—Zhao Ren

Things needed according to individual abilities and habits are called living standards, and the expenditure to maintain this standard is called living expenses.

Living standards are the things that each person needs at the current time and place. There are many other things that have not yet satisfied desires, so living standards can be raised and expanded at any time and place according to the promotion of each person's ability. From an individual point of view, the expansion of the need for things is the result of individual effort. From the perspective of the whole, the driving force of social progress is based on individual efforts to satisfy the needs of things beyond the current living standards. In the past history and current society, the operation and competition of people from all walks of life, whether their methods are proper or not, are all dissatisfied with the current living standards and hope to enjoy things that have never been enjoyed before. From an economic point of view, the disputes and separations between countries are nothing more than a symbol of striving to improve the general living standards of their own countries and expand the needs of things.

However, within a certain period and a certain region, the things included in the living standards have obvious differences in fineness, roughness, beauty, ugliness, quantity, and quality. The elements that determine it are three points. One is social class. The definition of the word "class" has always been very general. There are common divisions into upper, middle, and lower classes, into rich and poor classes, into labor and capital classes, and into mental and manual labor classes, etc. Although the meanings are very different, the main idea implicitly contains the difference between high and low, which is actually inappropriate. We believe that since the word "class" has been used for a long time and is not convenient to abandon, it should be distinguished in the economic dictionary exclusively according to occupation. Because of different occupations and the different environments in which they are located due to their occupations, the things needed are also different. For example, the clerk in the bank, the foreman in the factory, and the middle school teacher have roughly the same income. However, the bank clerk must take looking good and being able to socialize as the norm, so clothing must be paid special attention to. The needs of middle school teachers are in books. The foreman's short clothes and trousers are not different, and what he needs is somewhere else. It is not only because of his occupation that he is forced to do so, but his environment changes with his occupation, and he is transformed imperceptibly. Second is income. The more income, the wider the horizons and the greater the desires. Food and drink cannot be increased sharply, but the quality must be more refined than before. Other things that are not currently included in the living standards must be gradually introduced. When income shrinks, the things that are quietly consumed, regardless of quality or quantity, must be reduced. Third is the progress of material civilization. What was previously unavailable is now available. What was previously unattainable is now available for purchase at a lower price due to the mass production of machinery and the convenience of land and water transportation. Today's Western-style houses are far more comfortable than the tall and cold palaces. How many families could afford cars twenty years ago or telephones thirty years ago? How could you dream of electric lights and telephones in inland cities ten years ago? Now, although they are not popular, they should not be surprised as a strange story. Therefore, the so-called living standards are not only changing in quantity and quality, but also the things included in it are constantly changing and alternating.

Then, are there differences between high and low in living standards, as commonly said? We believe that the word "high," whether interpreted as noble or noble, is inappropriate. Those who live in Western-style houses, go out in cars, and need servants for all their actions can be said to be noble. Sitting quietly in a humble room, eating vegetables and wearing cloth clothes, not asking about honor or disgrace, and not fighting with the world, can be said to be noble. However, we only recognize the former as luxury and the latter as quirky, as personal peculiarities. What is most likely to affect the future of a country is the lowest living standard and the appropriate living standard. The so-called lowest living standard must include food, clothing, and housing, so that they have the lowest quantity and quality to maintain their survival and work efficiency. In addition to proper nutrition, warmth, and daily life, an appropriate living standard must have other things, such as education, books, and good social and entertainment, to stimulate intellectual, physical, and cultural contributions. If the low living standards cannot be maintained, the children and grandchildren will be weak and dull, and if they die unfortunately, the population will decrease. If appropriate living standards cannot be maintained, they will either flow into arrogance, luxury, and debauchery, or they will lose themselves in ignorance and hardship. Neither is a way to improve the nation.

In addition, after the living standard is determined by the individual and its environment, the force to continue to maintain or further expand the previous living standard can affect the increase or decrease of the population. The standards we are talking about are not only for individuals but also include family members who are supported by them. Marriage and childbirth are natural principles, but the education of children takes time, and the increase in individual income is limited. Even if the individual can maintain the previous living standard, or even expand it greatly, it is difficult to guarantee that their children and grandchildren can maintain the current standard and not fall into disgrace. Therefore, those with a little foresight are either worried about their own old age or worried that their children and grandchildren will fall into poverty and lowliness, and they will control childbirth in advance. The titles and properties of British aristocrats are only passed on to the eldest son, the old custom in China is that the eldest son occupies a larger share of the inheritance, and the universal late marriage and birth control in France, although in different ways, are intended to maintain a certain living standard throughout the generations. The impact on the population is most evident in France, which has been stagnant at around 40 million people for a long time. On the contrary, in China in recent decades, due to domestic and foreign political and economic turmoil, social income has obviously shrunk, but the population has continued to increase as in the past. Therefore, the general living standards have to continue to fall for a long time. The life of ordinary farmers today is actually on the verge of or has fallen below the starvation line. This is well known and is the reason why the talk of rural relief is so prevalent.

Page 7

Roosevelt's Message to Congress: New Budget Revenues and Expenditures Do Not Offset, Agricultural Adjustment Act Ineffective, Tax Revenue Greatly Reduced, Silver Coinage Tax Reflects Future Silver Purchase Policy 56

Expansion of the Air Force Requires Expenditures of 80 Million

Washington - Roosevelt's 1937 budget was already unable to offset revenues and expenditures before it was submitted to Congress. After the Agricultural Adjustment Act became ineffective, the President's original estimate of $547,000,000 in business tax revenue was no longer based on anything. Even the $529,000,000 included in the 1936 budget only collected $64,000,000. (Guomin, 6th)

Washington - The government is about to submit the 1937 budget, in which, regarding the air force, the government proposes to build 884 warplanes with an expenditure of 58 million US dollars, of which 507 are for the army and 377 are for the navy. It is generally believed that part of these planes are to replace old planes, so the total number of US military planes in 1937 will not increase much compared to the past. (Havas, 6th)

Washington - President Roosevelt's budget message to Congress today stated that the government predicts that the Treasury's silver coinage tax in the 1937 fiscal year will be sharply reduced compared to this year. Experts here therefore speculate that the US Treasury will purchase less silver than before, and that the silver price paid will be lower than the average price this year. According to the President's estimate, the Treasury's coinage tax is sufficient to reflect the amount of silver purchased under the Silver Purchase Act and the Silver Nationalization Act. In 1937, it will only increase by $600,000,000, compared to $161,088,000 this year and $140,110,000 last year. According to the budget estimate, $370,000,000 in coinage tax will be available by the end of 1937, compared to $310,000,000 by the end of 1936. The coinage tax paid for most of the new metal ore being silver will yield $19,000,000, compared to an estimated $20,000,000 this year and $58,000,000 in 1934. (Guomin, 6th)

Opposition Faction Greatly Rejoices Upon Hearing the News 57

Washington - The Republican Party and the New Deal opposition faction were very satisfied with the Supreme Court's recent ruling that the Agricultural Adjustment Act violated the Constitution, believing that the Roosevelt government had suffered another fierce blow. It is generally believed that various laws related to the Agricultural Adjustment Act, such as the Bankhead Cotton Act, the Smith Tobacco Act, and the Warren Potato Act, will be declared invalid by the Supreme Court next week. According to observations from some people, President Roosevelt had previously considered proposing an amendment to the current Constitution when the Supreme Court declared that the regulations of the Economic Recovery Bureau violated the Constitution (in June last year), but then gave up. Now that the Agricultural Adjustment Act has been declared invalid, it will inevitably be brought up again and require major amendments. Even the message that the President read to Congress yesterday stated that the "privileges" enjoyed by Congress can be protected by devising a way. This statement was aimed at the Supreme Court. In addition, government spokespersons have recently repeatedly declared that the American people are free to amend the national fundamental law if they wish to do so, indicating the President's intention to request an amendment to the Constitution. (Havas, 6th)

Authorities Discuss Remedial Measures 58

Washington - President Luo declined to criticize the Supreme Court's verdict and is currently discussing it with Agriculture Secretary Wallace and Attorney General Cummings. It is widely expected that President Luo will use financial assistance to persuade the states to adopt their own laws to replace the current law that has been ruled invalid in order to achieve the original purpose of supporting rural villages. After hearing the verdict of the Supreme Court, General Johnson, the initial administrative commissioner of the new measures, said that if the court ruled that all methods of the US government to relieve rural areas were illegal, the authorities would have no other choice but to fight on the constitutional issue. According to government sources, the income of American farmers in 1935 increased by 110 million yuan, which was due to the Agricultural Adjustment Act. (Reuters, 6th)

Washington - After the Supreme Court announced its verdict that the Agricultural Adjustment Act was invalid, there was much speculation about President Luo's upcoming movement, but it was widely expected that the authorities were well prepared and could act immediately. However, judging from the phenomenon, there may not be any action immediately. Although President Luo did not express his opinion on this verdict, he will consult with the leaders of the government on everything, and there may be a concrete announcement in three or four days. It is reported that the government owes farmers 500 million yuan in subsidies in accordance with existing contracts. Government lawyers say that this expenditure must be paid regardless of the fate of the Agricultural Adjustment Act. It is reported that President Luo and his staff have now planned to request the allocation of funds to pay off the funds that farmers should receive under the existing Agricultural Adjustment Act contract up to the date of the court's verdict.

At the same time, political observers are now quite doubtful about the fate of the Social Security Act, the Guffey Coal Act, and the Wagner Labor Disputes Act, etc., because these bills are all based on Congress's unlimited authority. Agriculture Secretary Wallace and his staff are all in their offices studying the extent to which the Agricultural Adjustment Act has been irreparably destroyed. Republican Senator McNani is currently planning a new rural bill, the main purpose of which is to restore the subsidy method for agricultural product exports. At the same time, several members of parliament advocate amending the Constitution. Business people, in view of today's verdict of the Supreme Court, believe that the Peng Head case and the Tobacco case being ruled invalid is expected, and cotton merchants are now extremely anxious about the handling of the cotton stored by the US Cotton Reserve Agency after the Peng Head case is ruled invalid in the future. Agriculture Secretary Wallace and Agricultural Adjustment Bureau Director Davis are prepared to immediately submit a new bill to Congress. It is reported that the authorities plan to provide central assistance to the states so that each state can establish its Agricultural Adjustment Act and achieve its original purpose. (Reuters, 6th)

Impact on the Future Presidential Election 59

Washington - Some members of Congress today predicted that this session of Congress will be extended to Christmas this year due to the Supreme Court's ruling that the Agricultural Adjustment Act (AAA) is unconstitutional, pending the conclusion of the presidential election. Many supporters of the New Deal measures said that most of the New Deal policies have lost their vitality. The new Social Security Act, which provides for unemployment insurance, old-age pensions, and work relief programs, will also be ruled invalid for the same reasons. Politics is now in great chaos. Funding for assisting farmers in limiting production, totaling 113 million yuan, ceased flowing last night, and office staff will therefore be laid off. Officials at the Agricultural Adjustment Administration (AAA) have not yet commented on this situation, but it is rumored that the AAA is now considering the following three temporary alternative measures:

* Domestic distribution program that insures prices for farmers based on the amount of production.

* Establishing 48 small-scale state AAAs under central coordination.

* Providing subsidies to farmers who properly use their land.

Political leaders generally say that the Supreme Court's decision will have a significant impact on the presidential election campaign. Even if Congress can levy new taxes to meet the current expenses of agricultural production restriction contracts, Congress is very reluctant to do so in light of future elections. Those who generally welcome the Supreme Court's decision are now unusually silent, because the issue of rural relief is extremely important, and farmers' votes are considered extremely important by both the Republican and Democratic parties. (Reuters dispatch, 7th)

The Constitution Needs Amendment More Than Ever 60

Washington - After the Supreme Court's ruling, Agriculture Secretary Wallace immediately held a closed-door meeting with his staff, and then announced the cessation of collecting donations based on the AAA. According to opinions from Congress, if the government wants to preserve the social order created by President Roosevelt and prevent its complete demise, it will have to use amending the Constitution as a tool for competitive elections. Many Democratic members believe that the repeated blows to the agricultural and industrial sectors from the Supreme Court's rulings on the New Deal measures will inevitably lead to increased anxiety. American Federation of Labor President Green stated that the Constitution now needs amendment more than ever. The Supreme Court's decision has made the agricultural and industrial sectors aware of the difficulties under the limitations of the Constitution. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

Stock Market in Great Turmoil 61

New York - After the Supreme Court's decision on the AAA was announced, the national securities and commodities exchanges were in great turmoil. Initially, there was a frenzied buying of cotton and wheat, but then, in a sudden change of heart, people sold them off one after another, and the market situation was very chaotic. Wheat initially rose by two points, and cotton rose by more than one yuan per bale, but before long, most of the gains were lost. Grain stocks on the New York Stock Exchange initially rose by one to three pounds, but sales of farm equipment and commodity stocks soon rose, fearing that rural purchasing power would be weakened by the decision. The majority opinion of Wall Street merchants is that the government will soon propose new legislation to prevent rural purchasing power from being greatly affected. At the same time, merchants of gold, silver, food, and cotton textiles welcomed the Supreme Court's decision, believing that prices could be reduced and consumption increased as a result. Wall Street insiders predict that the recovery movement will not suffer a major setback as a result of this, because the people will be able to quickly adapt to their environment. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

Cotton and Wheat Exports Expected to Increase 62

Washington - A local authority on Far Eastern trade issues predicted today that the Supreme Court's blow to the U.S. agricultural control program may increase U.S. cotton, wheat, and tobacco exports to Eastern countries. This increase in exports is due to the reduction in costs after the abolition of the processing tax, which allows Far Eastern importers to obtain cheap goods. Experts claim that there has been a substantial decrease in U.S. exports of cotton, wheat, and tobacco to China and Japan from 1932, when production was unrestricted, to 1935, when agricultural production was controlled and processing taxes were levied. However, officials indicated that prices could have fallen more quickly, but this was due to the accumulation of large stockpiles three years ago, which were largely consumed during the control period. The United States has abundant production capacity and will soon be able to produce large quantities of food, but only if the government finds a way to limit its output can this be prevented. (National Telegram, 6th)

Philippine Commerce Not Expected to be Affected 63

Washington - Responsible businessmen in the Philippines declared today that the U.S. Supreme Court's ruling that the AAA is invalid will not harm the Philippines. On the contrary, after the situation calms down, it may generate commercial benefits. It is generally believed that the authorities should quickly correct the chaos in the situation. As a result of this chaos, the current procedures may be shelved because they favor Cuba more than the Philippines. The question now is whether we will restore the tariff on sugar that existed before the establishment of the Agricultural Adjustment Administration after the processing tax is ruled illegal, because this tariff had been reduced in order to offset the processing tax. Responsible parties believe that the Supreme Court's decision will not hinder the transfer of coconut oil tax revenues to the Philippine government, because the basis for this tax is a tax law rather than the AAA. However, the issue of collecting this tax is currently under review by the Colombian Supreme Court. (National Telegram, 6th)

Spanish Parliament Dissolved; General Election to be Held on the 16th of Next Month 64

Madrid - President Zamora recently ordered the extension of the adjournment of the Chamber of Deputies, and has now signed an order dissolving the chamber. The date of the re-election, the first vote is scheduled for February 16th, and the second round of voting is scheduled for March 1st. The newly elected members of the Chamber of Deputies are scheduled to convene on March 16th. (Havas dispatch, 7th)

A communique was then issued stating that, according to this agreement, the total value of French goods exported to the Soviet Union each year should be equal to that of Soviet goods imported into France, but Soviet kerosene imported into France is not included in this provision. Overseas Correspondence

Ceylon, a Sacred Buddhist Land 66

On November 20th, 1935, the reporter took advantage of a study tour to Europe and visited Ceylon for half a day. This place is a sacred Buddhist land, anciently known as the Lion Kingdom. There are many historical sites and cultural relics worth recording. Here's my account:

Ceylon is an island southeast of the Indian peninsula, separated from the mainland by a strait. Many coral islands are scattered in the strait like a bridge, called Adam's Bridge. Its location is 81 degrees east longitude and 7.5 degrees north latitude, in the tropics. The climate is very hot, with no so-called seasons. The population is more than 5,303,000, mostly brown-skinned, of Indo-European descent. It is now a directly administered British colony. The capital, Colombo, is on the southwest coast of the island, a key point on the Europe-Asia sea route. Important products of the island, such as rubber, coconuts, tea, ebony, and graphite, are all exported from here. The old capital, Kandy, is in the mountains in the center of the island, 72 miles from Colombo. There are many ancient temples and famous sites. Legend has it that Sakyamuni once came here to preach. There is a Bodhi tree, which is a branch from the first sacred tree in India (Sakyamuni attained enlightenment under the tree, hence it is called Bodhi. Bodhi is a Sanskrit word meaning enlightenment). The original tree in India is now gone. This old trunk, more than two thousand years old, still stands majestically. There is also a Buddha tooth, kept in the Buddha hall, said to have been left by Sakyamuni.

Because the reporter was on the same ship with the Ceylonese High Monk Narada (Hikkbu Narada), he disembarked in Colombo for a visit. He was introduced by him to a local benefactor named JR. Jayawerdena, who took care of everything. We first went to the Buddhist Library, then visited several Buddhist temples, decided to tour the city streets, and finally had lunch at Jayawerdena's house. After the meal, because Mr. Jayawerdena had other business, we sat and chatted briefly and parted happily.

The Buddhist Library is located in Vajirarama, Bambalapitiya. There is a master in charge, about fifty years old. His Dharma name seems to be Sasada. The collection is limited to Buddhism and Buddhist studies. There are thousands of books, mostly in Sanskrit and English. The resident monks are mostly able to devote themselves to research. Master Narada has written many books. One of his Buddhist studies has a translated version in the Shanghai Buddhist Pure Land Society. Master Narada decided to travel east this time, traversing China, Japan, Singapore, Java and other places. His main purpose was to escort a branch of the Bodhi sacred tree of Ceylon to China for transplantation, so as to promote Buddhism. He also inspected the current state of Buddhism in the East. He was well received by fellow Buddhists in Shanghai. He was presented with many farewell poems.

In Ceylonese customs, one must put one's palms together and kneel down to pay respect to the Dharma Master. One must take off shoes and hats outside the door before entering the temple. One must offer freshly picked fragrant flowers when worshiping the Tathagata. One must not pick fresh leaves when admiring the Bodhi sacred tree. The reporter went to several temples to pay respects and followed the customs meticulously. As a result, I was able to see the sacred sites and feel very fortunate. What I saw and heard in the Buddha hall was very different from what I've seen in China:

* The construction of the hall is octagonal. There are no pavilions or lofts. Only concentric octagonal layers, painted and sculpted with Buddha statues. The scale is small, lacking the majestic style represented by our Lingyin Buddha Hall.

* The Tathagata Buddha statues are as beautiful as women, and the ears have traces of earrings. The ears are elongated, and the holes are also elongated.

* The Tathagata Buddha is the center of faith. There are no statues of Maitreya, Arhats, Avalokiteśvara, Skanda, Manjushri, Samantabhadra, etc.

* There are many murals, all oil paintings. The paintings depict the life and miracles of the Tathagata Buddha, lifelike. The statues also represent the Buddha's preaching and miraculous deeds. The figures are realistic, and the back and sides of the statues are painted on the walls, making them even more vivid. The statues and paintings all have a Western European style.

* Fresh flowers are offered, clean and tidy, with no turbid smell of incense, candles, or paper money.

* There is only a giant bell, but no wooden fish, chimes, drums, or other noisy instruments.

* One must take off shoes and hats outside the door before entering the temple.

* Lectures on the scriptures are open to the public and anyone can listen.

* There are many Westerners who believe in Buddhism. There are Buddhist halls built by Westerners (one named D. Ddward H. Pedris, who was a government official and a Buddhist, was murdered on July 7, 1915. His parents specially built a grand Buddhist temple area, including a Buddha hall, lecture hall, pagoda, dining hall, monks' quarters, sacred tree, etc. There are many marble offering tables donated by other Westerners in the hall). Most of those who come to worship are Westerners.

There are only two or three points that are the same as in China:

* Palms together and kneeling.

* There are also monks in the empty door who do not abide by the rules and secretly eat meat.

* Bald head wearing a cassock (actually just a piece of cloth wrapped around the body), with no burn marks on the head.

Sakyamuni Buddha was born in 623 BC, a prince of the Kapilavastu Kingdom of Central India. His clan was Sakyan, his name was Siddhartha Gautama. At the age of sixteen, he married Princess Yasidhara and lived in peace and prosperity for thirteen years. At the age of twenty-nine, he began to practice asceticism for six years. One day, he sat under the Bodhi tree and suddenly had an epiphany, thus attaining Nirvana. However, although Buddhism originated in India, it is not prevalent in India today. On the contrary, it occupies a considerable influence in Ceylon, Myanmar, China, and Japan. Is it not true that what is lost in the rites is sought in the wilderness?

The streets of Ceylon are very clean. There are coconut palms and small landscaped trees with many spotted leaves along the roadside. The residences are extremely small and exquisite, and every house must have a garden. Mr. Jayawerdena's residence is excellent. In our eyes, it can be called a cool villa. Although the house is only one story high, the layout is well-organized and the furnishings are beautiful. Mr. Jayawerdena lives with his mother, wife, brother, and sister. They are all respectful and polite to guests, as they have all received secondary education. Before the meal, Mr. Jayawerdena first offered me lemonade and coconut water, and gave me a few Bodhi leaves and a copy of "The Life of Buddha" (written by Master Narada and published by Mr. Jayawerdena). During the meal, I tried the local Ceylonese flavor. Both meat and vegetarian dishes are added with curry. Using my fingers instead of knives and forks, I put the rice and dishes into my mouth. It was quite interesting to return to simplicity. After the meal, I ate papaya and fragrant bananas and drank double-steamed water from a clay pot (the method is to put boiled water in a clay pot and wait for it to cool, then boil it again in the pot, so it is rich in earthy and smoky flavors. It would be impolite to refuse, so I had to frown and swallow it). After this meal of exotic flavors, I said goodbye.

Ceylonese men's clothing: a cotton yarn shirt on the upper body, a skirt on the lower body, and bare feet. Some are naked with a triangular cloth. The middle and upper classes mostly wear Western suits. Women wear only a halter-style short shirt on the upper body, with wide shoulders, bare arms, and high breasts exposed outside the clothing, with a rich curvy beauty. The lower body is a colored skirt and bare feet. The clogs or slippers are a combination of Chinese and Japanese styles. The middle and upper classes who wear Western clothing have the same trends as men.

The Ceylon municipal administration is good. Under the British government's management, the construction is also quite remarkable. As for the administration, they used to treat the natives harshly, but now, due to the influence of Gandhi's efforts in India, it is more relaxed than before. There are not many Chinese businessmen here. They are mostly silk merchants. The Ceylonese currency, the rupee, is approximately equal in value to the Chinese currency at the current exchange rate.

The Italian ship Conte Rosso also arrived the day before the reporter arrived in Ceylon. Because the League of Nations implemented economic sanctions, there were many difficulties in renting boats, inspecting goods, and restricting the purchase of oil. It is said that they were quite embarrassed for a while. (Xu Zhenchi from Suez, December 1, 1935)

Page 8

U.S. AAA Ruled Unconstitutional 67

Agricultural Controls Also Completely Overturned

Another Blow to Roosevelt's New Deal

Washington - The U.S. Supreme Court today ruled the AAA, on which the entire agricultural program of the New Deal was based, unconstitutional. The law has failed following the National Industrial Recovery Act (NIRA), marking one of the most important pages in American judicial history. The appellant was Hoosac Mills Corporation, which claimed that the processing tax on cotton products was unconstitutional. Only three of the nine Supreme Court justices, those known as liberals, dissented. The majority opinion was led by Chief Justice Hughes and Justice Van Devanter, among six others. Justice Roberts, who usually holds liberal views, surprisingly read the majority opinion today, stating that controlling agricultural production, even through voluntary agreements and with government subsidies, is ultimately unconstitutional. The court said that this plan uses the federal government's funds to "purchase the obedience of the people." Roberts also said that if this theory can be maintained, then the government can use its power to tax to any state and redistribute the local industry population. Roberts also mentioned the Bankhead Cotton Control Act, which is awaiting judgment, saying that the law has more enforcement power than the AAA. Now that the AAA has been ruled invalid, all processing taxes on agricultural products such as wheat, rice, tobacco, sugar, and paper, and the entire system of agricultural control, have become illegal. In addition to the Hoosac case, there are 1,356 other cases nationwide where cotton and wheat mills are attacking processing taxes in local courts. The general opinion here is that the Supreme Court's decision is more serious for President Roosevelt's recovery program than the overturning of the NIRA, because after the ruling, the government cannot collect processing taxes on basic commodities, and its debts of millions of dollars to farmers will be impossible to pay off, and the AAA will have to be dissolved like the NIRA. After the judgment was announced, the White House said that the president had no comment for the time being. Observers said that the wording of the decision was very firm and it would be difficult for the government to find another alternative. (National Telegram, 6th)

Washington - The AAA, promulgated by the government on May 12 last year, has recently been ruled unconstitutional by the Supreme Court. The verdict states, "This law endangers the rights of each state." According to the Constitution, although the government may collect taxes to promote the general welfare of citizens, it has no right to use special means to assist agriculture. The verdict also states that the court's task is to judge whether the government is executing the law according to law, and not to question whether the law is wise. It said, "If voters think that a certain law is not very good, they can advocate its abolition." Regarding the agricultural problem, Congress allowed the government to collect agricultural product processing taxes in order to "achieve an illegal and unconstitutional purpose," which is a means to "use federal public funds" to win over farmers and make them comply with federal law. In fact, this kind of problem belongs to the legislative scope of each state, not to be handled by the federal government. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

Washington - The AAA was promulgated on May 12 of last year. Its purpose was to allow the government to help farmers during agricultural panics, thereby increasing their purchasing power. On the one hand, it also supplemented the relief fund so that it could cope with all difficulties during economic changes. The specific method was for the government to establish the AAA to limit the planting area of various agricultural products. All farmers who reduced their production were given subsidies. Since the establishment of the AAA last May, the subsidies and relief funds allocated to farmers have reached 100 million U.S. dollars. Processing taxes on agricultural products are levied on farmers receiving subsidies in order to compensate for part of the expenditure. Although farmers and the AAA have signed contracts to accept production restriction measures, they have mostly expressed opposition to the processing tax and have filed lawsuits in court, claiming that what the government is doing violates the Constitution. As of last July, there have been more than 160 such cases. The Boston Court of Appeals once ruled that this tax was unconstitutional. At that time, in addition to appealing to the Supreme Court, the government also sent Senator La Follette to Congress to propose an amendment to the AAA, advocating that the power of the Minister of Agriculture to control the production and distribution of agricultural products be expanded in order to prevent the people from accusing the government of violating the Constitution again. This amendment was passed separately by the House and Senate, but the Supreme Court recently ruled that the AAA violates the Constitution, so the processing tax, which the AAA relies on as its only source, must be abolished. As for the contracts signed by the AAA with farmers to restrict production, the subsidies that should be paid to the farmers must still be paid, and the government only needs to find new sources of funding to cope with it. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

Washington - Since the Supreme Court ruled that the AAA is unconstitutional, the AAA has recently stopped collecting processing taxes on agricultural products and has temporarily stopped paying subsidies to farmers. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

Washington - Observers claimed today that after the Supreme Court ruled the AAA invalid, the Bankhead Cotton Control Act and the Kerr Tobacco Control Act, among other agricultural control bills, have been completely overturned. However, the government has signed various agricultural control contracts with farmers across the country, and must pay subsidies of 60.2 million U.S. dollars. Now that the processing tax cannot be collected, other taxes must be raised to pay off this debt. (National Telegram, 6th)

New Appointed American Advisor to the Abyssinian Emperor Arrives, Only 28 Years Old 68

Addis Ababa - Our correspondent, O'Chana, reports that the name of the new American advisor recently hired by the Abyssinian Emperor, which had been kept secret, has now been announced. He is named Spencer and arrived here from French Djibouti last night. He began his duties this morning. Spencer is only 28 years old. This decision to accept the appointment was recommended by Colson, the American financial advisor to the Abyssinian government. (Havas dispatch, 7th)

It is rumored that he has been hired by the government as a specialized diplomatic advisor. However, the government is keeping his name and past qualifications a strict secret. It is expected that a detailed announcement will be made tomorrow. He recently left his post and returned to his country due to ill health. It is rumored that the newly hired American gentleman will fill the vacancy left by General Vilqin. Osaka Shosen Kaisha New Japan-Philippines Route 99

Chicago Maru and two other ships begin service

From Tokyo, Taiwan, Xiamen to Philippines

Xiamen correspondence: Japan's southward routes, in the past five or six years, only had the Taiwan-Keelung-Takao route via Xiamen, Shantou to Hong Kong, operated by Osaka Company's two ships and one ship between Taiwan and Fuzhou. Since last year (1935) it gradually expanded. During the Taiwan Exposition in the second half of the year, Osaka Company added four ships, Fengshan Maru, Di Li Maru, Guangdong Maru, and Twenty-Six Kyodo Maru, between Taiwan, Xiamen, Shantou, and Hong Kong. Another route was set up between Taiwan, Fuzhou, and Xiamen, using Daikyu Maru. At the same time, Nisshin Kisen Kaisha resumed its Shanghai, Xiamen, Hong Kong, and Guangzhou route, using Songshan Maru and Tangshan Maru. Since the winter, the Japanese military and the Governor-General of Taiwan convened a conference on tropical industries and a joint conference of the army, navy, and overseas Chinese in Taiwan, and decided to carry out a southward policy with Taiwan as the center, develop South China and Nanyang trade and shipping, and assist the economy of resident overseas Chinese. Regarding shipping, a new Nanyang route has been opened, first to Japan and the Philippines. The Xiamen branch of Osaka Shosen Kaisha recently received an order from the Japanese government to develop the Nanyang route. The head office has allocated three ships, Chicago Maru, Hikoji Maru, and Mexico Maru, with a deadweight of 5,000 to 7,000 tons. The route is from Tokyo via Osaka, Taiwan, Xiamen, to Manila, Cebu, Davao, and Legazpi in the Philippines as the final destination. Then, the return voyage from Legazpi will return to Japan. It is scheduled to start sailing at the beginning of this year. The first ship is Chicago Maru, which is scheduled to arrive in Xiamen on January 6 and then go to Manila. Hikoji Maru will pass Xiamen and open to the Philippines on January 22, and Mexico Maru will pass Xiamen and open to the Philippines on February 7. However, the three ships will pass through Xiamen on their southward voyage, while the northward voyage will return to Japan directly from the Philippines via Taiwan, without passing through Xiamen. (January 4)

Wuhu Public Accuses the Police Chief of Illegal Activities 100

Arbitrary Extortion of Large Sums of Money

All Sectors Telegraph Requests for Severe Punishment Wuhu correspondence: Zhang Zongfen, the chief of the Wuhu Public Security Bureau, has implemented measures since taking office that are quite unsatisfactory to the citizens. Since the government issued the smoking ban, all sectors have assisted in its implementation because it is an important policy for national recovery. However, Zhang often forced non-smokers to obtain licenses or exceeded the prescribed amount of fines and arbitrarily imposed punishments. He even detained and punished non-smoking people with some assets at any time and place, causing everyone to be in danger. Last month, the Henan Hongda Chang Sauce Garden was burned down, killing eleven men, women, and children. However, Zhang actually detained Zhang Taisong, the young owner of the shop who had suffered a great disaster, and forced him to pay a fine of 600 yuan. At the same time, Li Zhizhi, the head of the Second Branch of the Bureau, also arrested Li Peizhi, the son of the former Wuhu Customs Superintendent Li Baoling and a committee member of the Hunan Fellow Villagers Association, falsely accusing him of smoking and fining him 220 yuan. A few days later, he was ordered to pay a reward of 30 yuan. Li painfully complied because he was told that if he did not comply, he would be paraded through the streets and sent to the head office, but because he did not smoke and had suffered such humiliation, he filed a complaint with the county party headquarters. As a result, public sentiment was aroused, and the party headquarters, the lawyers' association, and all industries in Wuhu elected representatives and held joint meetings at the county chamber of commerce. Each meeting was attended by hundreds of people. The first resolution of the conference was to report the facts of Zhang's corruption and the imminent civil unrest to the central government and departments, requesting them to send personnel to investigate and order the bureau chief to publicly announce all the fine accounts. Gao Tiejun, the former commissioner, Tao Yutang, a standing committee member of the chamber of commerce, Fang Dingzhong, the president of the lawyers' association, and other twelve people were elected as general representatives to petition the administrative commissioner's office and other institutions. At this point, Zhang, realizing that he could not offend public anger, immediately ordered Chief Li to run around asking for mediation and returned the illegally fined amount of 400 yuan from Hongda Chang and a promissory note for 200 yuan that had already been collected. Upon receiving the news, all sectors became even more resentful and held a general meeting at the county chamber of commerce on the afternoon of the fifth. Even more people attended. First, lawyer Hu Jiaxin reported the truth about the public security bureau chief's cruel and unreasonable fine on Hongda Chang and the recent return of the promissory note, saying that the lawyers' association had decided to file a lawsuit according to law to uphold human rights. At that time, the whole venue applauded. It was resolved to ask Administrative Inspector Gao Wenbo to report in public. He said briefly that after interviewing the petition representatives and reading the newspapers, he had summoned Zhang to the office to inquire about Zhang's disturbance of the people with the smoking ban. Zhang replied that the fire fine for Hongda Chang was 400 yuan, and the fine for smoking was 400 yuan. He had just heard that the promissory note had been returned. He did not understand this matter yet. In short, corrupt officials should be severely punished according to law, and Wuhu had caused public resentment due to the smoking ban, which was extremely rare among officials. Today, the people's sentiment is so enthusiastic, and he strongly agrees, but there must be concrete methods to do it so that this matter will never happen again in the locality, etc. After deliberation, the meeting passed resolutions to send telegrams to the Executive Yuan, the Control Yuan, the Henan-Anhui Pacification Headquarters, the Anhui Provincial Government, the Anhui-Jiangxi Supervisory Envoy's Office, the Nanjing Smoking Ban Inspection Headquarters, the National Smoking Ban Committee, the Military Affairs Commission, and the Fellow Villagers Association in Beijing. The original text of the telegrams is recorded below: "Nanjing: Separately reported to Chiang, President of the Executive Yuan, Yu, President of the Control Yuan, Feng, Vice Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission, the Smoking Ban Headquarters, the National Smoking Ban Committee, Gu, Director of the Chongqing Executive Headquarters, Liu, Director of the Kaifeng Henan-Anhui Pacification Office, Liu, Chairman of the Anhui Provincial Government, Miao, Anhui-Jiangxi Supervisory Envoy, Fang Zhi, Anhui Fellow Villagers Association in Beijing, and all fellow villagers for their consideration: We respectfully observe that the banning of smoking and drugs is an important policy for national recovery, and the people should respectfully and diligently follow it. However, after Zhang Zongfen, the director of the Wuhu Public Security Bureau, took office, he condoned the police, arbitrarily arrested people, and imposed arbitrary fines, all outside the scope of the law. Taking the implementation of tobacco household registration as an example, if someone is privately smoking drugs, they should be dealt with according to the law. However, the bureau chief has extorted large sums of money from families with some assets in the city who do not smoke, arbitrarily forcing them to obtain licenses, using the smoking ban as a tool for extortion. The fines collected have never been issued a receipt, causing travelers to hesitate and everyone to be in danger. On December 31, local organizations held a joint meeting at the chamber of commerce and unanimously resolved that, in addition to the citizens who have been wronged collecting evidence and waiting for investigation, we should jointly report to you for your consideration and ask the Anhui Provincial Government to remove the bureau chief from office and investigate him to warn against corruption and reassure the people. We cannot help but pray. The rest are detailed in the report. Wuhu Lawyers' Association, County Chamber of Commerce, 58 Industry Associations, Chiefs of All Security Teams, Representatives of Real Estate, etc." Also, Li Peizhi, who was unjustly punished by the Second Branch for 250 yuan, has had his Hunan Fellow Villagers Association telegraph all parties, indignant and unable to calm down, requesting that justice be upheld. The local departments of the first, second, third, and fourth districts of Wuhu also held a joint meeting on the fifth and resolved that Cui Songgu, a comprador of the Sanbei Company, attended the smoking ban meeting previously convened by the Public Security Bureau. They ordered him to publicly announce what happened at that time and sent a letter to all parties' meetings, urging them not to compromise midway. Therefore, at the general meeting of all sectors, someone proposed that Commissioner Gao should first take custody of Zhang. (6th)

Songjiang

Bandits Send Letters to Scare and Extort Wealthy Households

Xiaokunshan in the fourth district of the county is near the Liuhe River, where bandits often appear. Now that it is severe winter, more than a dozen wealthy households have received threatening letters from bandits. The letters claim that funds are insufficient, and demand one or two hundred yuan or dozens of yuan. If they do not comply, they will use guns and bombs. Those who are brave ignore the letters, but those who are timid go to the meeting place specified by the bandits and pay the money to seek peace. It is heard that more than a dozen households in Xiaokunshan Town have been robbed because of their timidity.
