Wuxi

Police and Militia Force Refugees to Leave the Territory

In Tangping Township, Yinqiao area, the tenth district of the county, more than 160 refugees from Hunan arrived on New Year's Day and disturbed the peace. They went to the home of villager Zhou Yichun and robbed him of more than 320 yuan in silver, two gold buttons, and destroyed the door. Villagers sounded the gong to call for help, and the refugees fled in a panic, drowning Zhang Xiaofu and Zhang Xiaoqing. The court verified that they had fallen into the river and died. However, the refugees used this as an excuse to occupy the area. Feng Junyan, the chief of the mountain area, and the patrol officer of the Seventh Police Station of Yuqi reported to the county government's public security bureau. The bureau sent Inspector Wang, but his attempts to suppress the refugees were ineffective. A few days ago, the county government dispatched 72 soldiers from the Fourth Security Brigade, together with the Shijiuwan, Luoshe, and Zhou militias, the Yuqi Security Police Station, and Wang, the chief inspector of the Public Security Bureau, Ge, the inspector of the Public Security Bureau, the patrol officers of Yong Police District, and others, to suppress the refugees. The refugees insisted on demanding a court hearing before any action was taken, and then elected representatives Zhang Youcai and Yang Sien to meet with Long, the county magistrate, and Chen, the chief of the Public Security Bureau. County Magistrate Long persuaded them to leave the territory immediately and sent political police to accompany the refugee representatives, take a car to the countryside, gather more than a hundred strong men from the village to carry the luggage, and escort them to the city overnight. They stayed overnight at the Yansheng Temple, and were escorted out of the territory yesterday morning. The coffins of the two drowned refugees have been temporarily buried in the Shitouwan cemetery.

Some of the staff will be ordered to be eliminated immediately. The Zhejiang Construction Department Sericulture Control Committee was also decided by the Provincial Government meeting on the 7th to be transferred to the jurisdiction of the Provincial Government, with Zeng Yangfu still serving as the chairman of the committee. The powers of the committee have been increased, and it will be announced soon.

After the Centralized Issuance of Banknotes, Various Banks Closed Their Reserve Vaults 106

All Handed Over to the Issuance Reserve Management Committee for Safekeeping

Implementing the Inspection of Legal Tender Reserves to Demonstrate Great Faith

The Ministry of Finance announced that after stipulating that the banknotes of the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications would be legal tender from November 4, an Issuance Reserve Management Committee was established to centralize issuance. Now, all banks issuing banknotes, except for the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications, have complied with the order to close their issuing vaults and hand them over to the Reserve Committee for safekeeping. The details are as follows:

Complying with the Ministerial Order

The Ministry of Finance announced that: "Banknotes issued by banks other than the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications that have been approved for issuance and are currently in circulation are allowed to continue to be used as usual. The amount of issuance is limited to the total amount in circulation as of November 3 and shall not be increased. The Ministry will determine a deadline to gradually exchange them for Central Bank banknotes, and the statutory reserves of the total amount in circulation, together with the new banknotes that have been printed but not issued and the old banknotes that have been issued and recovered, shall be handed over to the Issuance Reserve Management Committee for safekeeping. The new banknotes that have been approved and are being printed shall also be handed over for safekeeping when they are printed." All banks issuing banknotes have now complied with the ministerial order.

Separate Inspections Completed

The banks issuing banknotes whose head offices are located in Shanghai are the Four Banks Reserve Vault (i.e., the China & South Sea Bank, the Continental Bank, the Yien Yieh Commercial Bank, and the Kincheng Banking Corporation), the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, the Commercial Bank of China, the Pih Ming Bank, the China Industrial Bank, the Agricultural and Commercial Bank of China, the China Agricultural and Industrial Bank, and the Reclamation Bank. As for the total amount of issuance and reserves, the Issuance Reserve Management Committee has already sent committee members such as Ye Zhuotang to complete separate inspections and completely handed them over to the vaults of the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications designated by the committee for safekeeping. All procedures have been completely completed before the end of December 1935.

Handling the Closing

A reporter from the New Voice News Agency visited Qian Xinzhi, Deputy General Manager of the Four Banks Joint Savings Society, yesterday morning. According to him, the Four Banks Reserve Vault was established for the issuance of banknotes by the four banks. Since the government reformed the currency system and centralized issuance, it complied with the ministerial order and handed it over to the Issuance Reserve Management Committee for safekeeping. There is no need for this vault to exist anymore, and it should be closed immediately. Moreover, the Zhejiang Industrial Bank and other banks issuing banknotes are handling it in the same way. As for the Four Banks Joint Savings Society, it will continue to operate as usual. According to reporters' inquiries at the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, the bank and others have handed over the banknotes and reserves they issued to the Issuance Reserve Management Committee for safekeeping, and the personnel of the issuance department have been either laid off or transferred to other departments.

Inspecting Legal Tender

Since the Ministry of Finance announced the inspection rules of the Issuance Reserve Management Committee, the committee has complied with the rules and implemented the inspection of the legal tender issuance amount and reserves of the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications, inspecting once a month, in addition to submitting reports to the Ministry of Finance for record and publicly announcing them monthly to demonstrate great faith. It is decided that after the Central Bank is reorganized into the Central Reserve Bank, it will specifically keep the reserves of various banks, manage the national treasury, and store all public funds, and will not engage in ordinary commercial banking business. After two years, it will enjoy the exclusive right to issue banknotes and become the bank of banks.

During the Final Closing Period, Monetary Conditions Were Relatively Loose 107

Banks to Announce Last Year's Profits Today

Sudden Increase in Applications for Industrial and Commercial Credit Loans

According to the New Voice News Agency, the final closing period for various industries in 1935 is approaching. Qian Zhuang and others are prepared, and monetary conditions are looser than in previous years. There has been a sudden increase in credit loan applications to the Industrial and Commercial Loan Review Committee. Banks will announce last year's profits today, which will be announced by the Guild. The details are as follows:

Monetary Conditions Looser

The Qian Zhuang Guild decided that after January 23 is the final closing period for 1935, all industries have prepared. Qian Zhuang tightened up all kinds of loans, such as credit mortgages, and paid attention to collection matters. They set the 15th as the settlement date for all business transactions. At the same time, due to the government's implementation of the new currency system policy and the bank's annual closing period, the market's monetary conditions are looser than in previous years. The Shanghai Qian Zhuang market's overnight interest rate was still 9% yesterday, that is, 9% daily interest per thousand yuan. The bank's reserve will yesterday's public bill interest rate was 10%, and the public bill discount rate was 15%.

Applying for Loans

The Industrial and Commercial Loan Review Committee has been handling small credit loans since August 1 last year. At the end of last month, during the bank's annual closing period, there was a sudden increase in applications for loans from domestic industrial and commercial firms. Now, because the final closing of various industries for 1935 is approaching, the number of applicants to the Loan Review Committee in recent days has increased compared to the bank's annual closing period. The Committee is very busy investigating. After the Standing Committee of the Committee approves, the loans will be approved.

Bank Profits After the banks closed their books for 1935, in the midst of this economic depression, all banks that are members of the Banking Association made profits. The Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications made the most. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency met with Secretary-General Lin of the Banking Association yesterday. According to him, the Association has sent letters to various members to investigate last year's profits, and many have reported to the Association one after another. After gathering the information, it will be published for unification. It is scheduled to collect all the information tomorrow (i.e., today) and officially announce it.

After the Method for Exchanging Legal Tender Was Agreed Upon, Foreign Banks Paid in Silver 108

The total is 30 million yuan, with Japanese banks accounting for 15%

The Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications Stabilize Foreign Exchange with Good Results

The Banking Association's Market Committee Has Been Abolished

According to the New Voice News Agency, after the Ministry of Finance allowed the silver and money industries to obtain legal tender from the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications with 60% silver and 40% guarantee, the method for foreign banks to pay in silver and exchange legal tender has been agreed upon, and various banks have complied with the regulations. Stabilizing foreign exchange has achieved good results, and the equalization tax has fallen. The details are as follows:

Methods for Foreign Banks to Exchange Legal Tender

After the Ministry of Finance agreed on the method for foreign banks to exchange silver for legal tender, various foreign banks exchanged their silver reserves for legal tender at par with the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications. Now, Citibank, the Netherlands Bank, and the Deutsche Bank have all paid in. Citibank paid in another 2.5 million yuan yesterday. HSBC, McCallum, and other banks will also pay in within days. As for Japanese banks, such as Yokohama Specie Bank, it is said that they have also agreed to pay in. The total amount of silver deposited by foreign banks is more than 30 million yuan, with Japanese banks accounting for 15%.

Stabilizing Foreign Exchange Has Achieved Good Results

After foreign silver prices plummeted, foreign banks restricted the buying and selling of foreign exchange. The foreign exchange trading of the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications increased sharply. Fortunately, after strenuous efforts to stabilize it, good results were achieved. Yesterday, the Central Bank quoted London at one shilling two pence and a half, New York at twenty-nine dollars seventy-five, and Paris at four hundred and fifty-one francs, which was equal to the previously determined standard number. HSBC quoted London at one shilling two pence three seven five, New York at twenty-nine dollars five, and Paris at four hundred and forty-seven francs. The equalization tax rate announced by the Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee yesterday morning has fallen to 7.75%, which has returned to the market conditions before November 4. All foreign banks have agreed to pay in silver to exchange legal tender, so taxpayers who transport silver for export have disappeared.

Bank Market Committee Abolished

Since the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications unconditionally traded foreign exchange, the Banking Association deleted Article 7 of the industry regulations, which published domestic and foreign market prices, and stopped publishing domestic and foreign market prices from January 4, abolishing the organization of the Market Committee. As for the Foreign Exchange Committee and the brokers and regulations for verifying foreign exchange, although they have not been abolished, in fact, banks that operate foreign exchange, such as the Zhejiang Industrial Bank and the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, will handle the buying and selling of foreign exchange according to the Central Bank's quotation in the future, only taking commissions.

Copper-Nickel Alloy Subsidiary Coins to Be Issued at the End of the Month The Mint Started Casting the Day Before Yesterday The Ministry of Finance Will Announce Their Circulation in the Market 109

The Ministry of Finance believes that there is a great need for subsidiary coins in various places after the implementation of legal tender. It has drafted a draft subsidiary coin ordinance, which has been submitted to the Central Political Committee for approval and to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation. Before the legislative process is completed, in order to regulate the market economy, it has been decided that the Central Mint will first cast six kinds of new subsidiary coins made of copper-nickel alloy: 50-cent, 20-cent, 10-cent, 5-cent, 2-cent, and 1-cent coins. The trial casting has been completed, and the shape and quality have been identified as qualified. Formal casting began the day before yesterday, and the coins will be issued at the end of the month. At that time, the Ministry of Finance will announce their official circulation in the market. After a larger number of coins have been cast, they will be transported to the branches of the Central Bank in various places for use.

The Jiangxi Provincial Department of Finance Borrows Two Million Yuan from the Three Banks Director Wu of the Department of Finance Comes to Shanghai to Negotiate and Discuss Providing Loans to Relieve the Economic Decline in Jiangxi Province 110

According to the Daily News, the Jiangxi Provincial Department of Finance, in view of the economic decline in Jiangxi Province in recent years and the sluggish noodle industry, has arranged for the Department of Finance to borrow two million yuan from the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications in Shanghai, which will be handled by the Jiangxi Provincial Yumin Bank to provide loans for relief. Director Wu of the province came to Shanghai from Jiangxi the day before yesterday to meet with Minister of Finance Kong and leaders of the banking community to discuss the loan. The methods are: The loan types are divided into two parts: (A) Goods mortgage: The borrower shall apply for a loan from Yumin Bank in accordance with the ordinary goods mortgage procedures, and then Yumin shall re-mortgage to the three banks. This type of goods is limited to those that can be effectively transferred and occupied. (B) If the goods cannot be transferred and occupied temporarily, the borrower shall provide real estate as a second guarantee, specify the type, quantity, and value of the goods, issue a note, and borrow from Yumin Bank, and then Yumin shall re-discount it to the three banks. The proportion of the aforementioned loans is 70% for A and 30% for B. Yumin shall re-mortgage and re-discount to the three banks after being reviewed and approved by the three banks. The loan term is limited to four months. If the loan cannot be repaid on time, the provincial government shall be requested to make special flexible regulations for the borrower and guarantor, and administrative sanctions shall be applied.

Taikoo Company's Rescue Ship Still Aground After Six Days of Rescue 114

The Taikoo Company's new Yangtze River ship Wuxue departed from Shanghai on the 31st of last month. On the afternoon of New Year's Day, while traveling near Shierxu above Zhenjiang, there was heavy rain and dense fog on the river, and the river water receded. The Wuxue ship suddenly ran aground. Due to the large amount of cargo and heavy draft, the bottom of the ship was deeply mired in shallow sand. For days, the company's upstream and downstream river ships have repeatedly towed it, but because the ship is grounded too deeply, it cannot get out of the shallow water. After receiving the telegram, the head office dispatched two iron barges to Shierxu on the 2nd of this month to prepare to gradually unload the cargo from the ship's various cabins. Yesterday, because there was more cargo and fewer barges, it dispatched another iron barge from Shanghai to the site to assist in unloading the cargo, so that the load could be reduced and the ship could float to the surface. Then, it could be towed again. Otherwise, if the river water continues to recede, it will be more difficult to escape. The cargo that has been unloaded will be transported to Wuhu by the upstream Changsha ship today and loaded with Wuhu cargo. Tomorrow, the export Juhu ship will go to load Hankou cargo.

Black Fever Has a Tendency to Spread to the Jiangnan Region; Chairman of the Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce Leng Yuqiu Came to Shanghai to Discuss Eradication Methods; Zhenjiang Hongren Hospital and Other Institutions Spent a Large Sum of Money to Engage in Eradication 120

Black fever has been found in the Jiangbei area and is spreading to various places. The disease is quite severe and has a tendency to affect the Jiangnan area. Leng Yuqiu, Chairman of the Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce, recently came to Shanghai to discuss eradication methods. It is heard that the local Hongren Hospital and other institutions have already spent a large sum of money to engage in eradication. The situation has been explored from the relevant aspects of this port, as follows. Black fever originated in the tropics. Patients have enlarged spleens. It was discovered in India and the Mediterranean coast in the 18th century. It then spread to Annam, Siam, the Philippines, the Caucasus, Turkestan, Asia Minor, the Americas, Panama, and North Africa. This disease was discovered in Hebei, Shandong, and other provinces in my country 30 years ago. At first, it was not noticed by the general public. In the 12th year of the Republic of China, it had already invaded Jiangsu Province, and the Xu, Huai, and Hai regions of Jiangbei were all affected. After the great flood in the 20th year of the Republic of China, the epidemic spread even wider. Patients with the disease are not easy to cure, and the number of deaths is increasing day by day. The harm is extraordinary. The central and provincial governments and other departments have successively organized investigation, research, and treatment institutions to actively carry out eradication. In recent years, although many people have been cured, the epidemic area has expanded, and the number of treatment institutions is limited. The spread has not been effectively controlled. In the future, the methods of prevention should be given extra effort. According to the investigation of the Black Fever Research Team, the disease spreads very quickly, increasing as much as 24 times in four years. Recently, the number of black fever patients diagnosed and treated by Zhenjiang Hongren Hospital has also been increasing day by day. Judging from this situation, the disease has crossed the Yangtze River to the south today. If this continues without being stopped, it will be easy for it to spread to Shanghai, where people from all over the world live, due to the convenience of the Beijing-Shanghai traffic. From Shanghai, it will spread to other places, which is truly frightening. For the sake of the present, in order to prevent the disease from affecting places where it has not yet been found, it is necessary to first eliminate the source of the disease in places where it has already occurred. In particular, it is necessary to widely publicize the transmission routes, symptoms, and treatments of the disease so that all places know how to take precautions.

Overseas Radio Telephone Communication; The International Telecommunications Bureau Is Actively Carrying Out; China-Japan Communication Is Scheduled to Be Implemented on February 15 122

Regarding the matters of radio telephone communication between China and Japan, China and the United Kingdom, etc., the reporter learned the following from the International Telecommunications Bureau yesterday:

China-Japan Communication Next Month 15th

Since the Ministry of Communications and the Japanese Ministry of Communications signed a contract last year, they have been actively carrying out communication for China-Japan radio telephones. It is now scheduled to be formally launched on February 15th. However, if preparations are not completed by then, the person in charge of the Telecommunications Bureau said that the date will be slightly delayed.

Principles for Deciding on Charging Methods

As for the charging methods for China-Japan communication, the principles have already been decided, that is, the charging for communication will generally be based on a three-minute standard. Regardless of whether the communication is one minute or two minutes, it will be charged according to three minutes. However, after three minutes, four minutes, five minutes, etc., will all be counted as four minutes and five minutes. Also, one second over three minutes will be counted as four minutes, and so on for four minutes, five minutes, six minutes, etc.

China-UK and China-US Are Actively Underway

As for communication with France, the UK, Italy, the US, and the Philippines, China-UK is actively underway and is in the testing phase. China-US and China-Philippines are also actively carrying out communication procedures, but have not yet been tested. China-France was tested once last year, and the results were very good, but it was temporarily suspended due to a lack of equipment. The Bureau is still actively preparing for communication with various countries and will communicate as soon as possible. The reason for the temporary suspension of communication with a certain country is actually due to insufficient equipment or other ongoing matters that have not yet been completed, so it has to be temporarily suspended.

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Instructs on Methods for Replacing and Affixing Stamps on Account Books; The General Closing Date Is the Principle; The Accounting Year Is the Exception 128

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce issued two letters yesterday regarding the annual replacement and affixing of stamps on account books, providing some explanations. Reply to Yong Sheng Yi Fertilizer Radio Company: "I received your letter on the 6th of this month, inquiring about the methods for replacing and affixing stamps on account books. I am now replying as follows: According to Article 10 of the Implementing Regulations of the Stamp Tax Law, regardless of when various account books subject to stamp tax begin to be used, the validity period of the stamp tax tickets affixed shall end on the date of the annual commercial closing of the year. If the accounts are closed according to the accounting year, the validity period shall end at the end of the accounting year. If they are continued to be used after the expiration date, new stamp tax tickets shall be affixed. The period for replacing and affixing stamp tax tickets on account books shall be based on the date of the commercial closing in principle and the accounting year as an exception. The two methods are at the discretion of the merchants and are not fixed. If your company's accounts are based on the accounting year from the Gregorian calendar New Year's Day to the end of December of the Gregorian calendar, at the end of the accounting year, either new account books are replaced, or old account books are continued to be used, and new stamps are affixed, which is not inconsistent with the provisions of Article 10 of the regulations." Reply to the Nanhui Town Business and People's Municipal Promotion Association: "I received your letter on the 6th of this month, inquiring about the matters of affixing stamp tax. I am now replying as follows: If the 24th year account books were opened before September 1 of the Gregorian calendar and the stamp was fully affixed at one corner in accordance with the old regulations, they can be used until the date of the commercial closing in accordance with the provisions of Article 10 of the Implementing Regulations of the Stamp Tax Law. If the old books are continued to be used after the expiration date, a stamp of two corners should be added in accordance with the law. The commercial closing date was originally January 31 according to the decision of the Executive Yuan, but the actual closing date this year is January 23, so there is no conflict with the statutory provisions to replace or add stamps from January 24. If the 'disclosure slip' mentioned in the letter is the collection slip used for the New Year's Festival, which only lists the amount of the outstanding balance and does not list the name, quantity, and price of the goods, it is not necessary to affix a stamp in accordance with Article 3, Section 9 of the Stamp Tax Law and Article 5 of the Implementing Regulations of the Stamp Tax Law. The 'disclosure book' mentioned in the letter is not known to what it refers. If it refers to the disclosure book for borrowing goods or accounts receivable and payable at ordinary times, then this disclosure book, whether it was opened before September 1 of the 24th year or after that date, cannot be exempted from affixing stamps in accordance with the old regulations and the new tax law. Therefore, the statement in the letter that it can be exempted from affixing stamps is a fundamental misunderstanding. The date for replacing stamps every year has been answered in detail in the first item above."

Notice from the Local Court: Important Information for Criminal Self-Suits 138

Chief Prosecutor Zhong Shangbin of the Shanghai Local Court Prosecutor's Office issued a notice yesterday stating that the Jiangsu High Court had forwarded a directive from the Ministry of Judicial Administration, emphasizing that the new Criminal Procedure Law has been in effect for some time, and the scope of self-suits has been greatly expanded compared to the past. However, people often cling to old habits and are unfamiliar with the new law, with many still filing complaints with the prosecutor's office when they should be initiating self-suits. Therefore, when local court prosecutor's offices receive cases that qualify for self-suits, they must follow previous orders, promptly instruct the complainants to file lawsuits directly with the court, and allow them to correct the original complaints and submit them directly to the court. The court must not refuse to accept the cases simply because the written complaint has been temporarily changed. This will make the self-suit system more effective and streamline the litigation process. In addition to instructing the prosecutor on duty when accepting cases, this notice is hereby issued to inform all litigants. Furthermore, the Local Court, to facilitate the understanding of the scope of self-suits for parties concerned, has separately recorded "Important Information for Self-Suits," listing each item in detail for easy reference. If any party concerned is unclear about self-suits, they can request a copy from the court's filing office. The full text of the "Important Information for Self-Suits" is recorded below: Anyone who is a direct victim of a crime and has legal capacity may file a self-suit. (This includes any individual who is a direct victim of a crime. For example, if an individual is directly victimized by a crime, even if their family or society is also victimized at the same time, the victimized individual may still file a self-suit.) To file a self-suit, a self-suit complaint must be submitted to the competent court, along with a copy of the complaint for each defendant. The self-suit complaint should include: (1) the defendant's name, gender, age, occupation, and characteristics; (2) the facts of the crime and evidence. If a complaint has already been filed, the words "complaint" can be changed to "self-suit," and the words "prosecutor" can be changed to "Criminal Division of the Court." A self-suit may not be filed against a direct ascendant relative or spouse. If a crime that is subject to prosecution or request is no longer eligible for prosecution or request, a self-suit may not be filed. (The phrase "no longer eligible for prosecution or request" refers to cases where a crime subject to prosecution has had the prosecution withdrawn, or a crime subject to request has had the request withdrawn after the six-month period for filing a request has expired.) A self-suit may not be filed if the same case has been concluded by the prosecutor's office. A person who withdraws a self-suit may not file a self-suit again.

Both Railways: Attention to Driving Safety – Orders Transmitted to Both Car and Machine Departments for Compliance 139

The Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureau received an order from the Ministry of Railways to pay close attention to driving safety. The bureau immediately ordered both the Car and Machine Departments to comply. The original text reads: The Ministry of Railways has issued a telegram stating that driving safety is the top priority for railways. Each railway association must assign the responsible section chiefs and stationmasters to inspect driving equipment such as electrical track circuits, track tokens, signals, and switches at any time. Driving personnel, such as drivers, stokers, brakemen, signalmen, and switchmen, must also be examined by the responsible personnel at any time. Driving personnel must not leave their posts while on duty. For example, drivers and stokers must not leave the locomotive, and brakemen must remain at their assigned positions to guard the brakes. All of the above items must be strictly followed. In addition to distributing this order, you are hereby ordered to instruct your subordinates to strictly comply.

Lunar Eclipse Today: Four Total This Year 142

According to the Central News Agency, there will be a lunar eclipse today (the 8th), which will be visible in its entirety across China. The initial eclipse will begin at 11:16 PM tonight, totality at 1:57 AM on the 9th, maximum eclipse at 2:00 AM on the 9th, the emergence from the umbra at 2:21 AM on the 9th, and the end of the eclipse at 5:01 AM on the 9th, providing ample opportunity for astronomical research. There will be a total of four lunar eclipses this year. This is the first. The second will be on June 19th, the third on July 14th, and the fourth on December 14th. Except for the fourth one, which will not be visible in China, the second and third will be partially visible in some parts of China.

Chen Zongyu, a court clerk from Shaoxing in the First Special District Court of Shanghai, had been married to Qi Hui, also from Shaoxing, for nearly ten years, but they had no children. The relationship between the couple was not harmonious. A conflict arose the previous summer, and the two became completely estranged. Disputes occurred frequently. In order to find solace and continue his lineage, Chen rented a house with a woman named Wang Nanzhen at No. 6, Lane 11, Beihe Road. However, he continued to provide living expenses for Qi. In January of that year, Wang became pregnant, and was three months along when Qi found out and went to make a scene, leading to a conflict. As a result, Wang miscarried. With the mediation of friends and relatives, a lawsuit was avoided. In the winter of that year, Chen and Qi both took sleeping pills in an attempt to commit suicide together. Fortunately, they were rescued in time. From then on, the animosity between the couple deepened. On the morning of the fourth of this month, Qi, accompanied by Chinese and foreign detectives from the Xinzha Police Station, went to No. 6, Lane 11, Beihe Road to catch Chen and Wang in the act of adultery. Both were arrested and sent to the criminal division of the First Special Court for interrogation. They were released on bail of 800 yuan each pending sentencing. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhan Liangce of the First Special Court issued a verdict in the Second Criminal Court, sentencing Chen Zongyu to two months imprisonment for adultery while married, and Wang Nanzhen to two months imprisonment for committing adultery. Both sentences were suspended for two years. Chen declared in court that he was not satisfied with the verdict and would appeal.

Russian Concierge Commits Suicide: Post-Mortem Examination; Body Claimed by the Russian Veterans Association 145

An old man by the translated name of Wulaoluofuluofu, 28 years old, the concierge of the Ruizhi Iron Factory at No. 516 Yangqiao Road, was known for his diligence and thrift, and was therefore highly trusted by the factory. At around 7 AM the day before yesterday, the Russian returned to the factory and walked to his bedroom. He suddenly raised his own pistol and fired a shot into his right temple, collapsing unconscious. After those in the factory heard the gunshot, they reported it to the Yulin Road Police Station, which dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to investigate. An ambulance was called to the scene and rushed him to Gongji Hospital, where he died without effect. The body was taken to the Feilun Road morgue. Yesterday morning, Tang, the prosecutor appointed by the First Special District Court, along with forensic doctor Zhang Yan and clerk Wang Zuyi, arrived at the morgue to examine the body. According to Western patrol leader Sidiwens, the deceased had been working at the Ruizhi Iron Factory since 1931, and his diligence was clear to all. However, he was fond of drinking. When the Meifeng Bank collapsed last year, the deceased lost over 700 yuan. The factory employs several Russian police officers, all of whom were under his management. On the 5th of this month, the factory issued 160 yuan for the Russian police officers' meals, which was given to him to distribute. However, he did not go on duty that night, but went out alone. He returned at around 7 AM the next morning and, while changing into his uniform in the bedroom, he suddenly told two other Russian police officers that he had used up not only his own money last night, but also the money for the other police officers' meals. Shortly after the two officers left, they heard a gunshot and immediately returned, finding him dead. According to Russian Yalishan Daofu, who works as a patrol leader at the Huishan Police Station, he had known the deceased for 18 years. They had served in the Russian army together. After the war broke out in Russia, they came to Shanghai together. They had formed a Russian Veterans Mutual Aid Association, with over 20 members, all of whom worked as bodyguards, watchmen, and other professions in Shanghai. As a committee member of the association, he knew that the deceased had no relatives in the world, so he represented the association and wished to claim the body for burial. Tang, having heard the statements, ordered that the deceased, Russian Wulaoluofuluofu, male, died from a self-inflicted gunshot wound to the head. The body was handed over to Yalishan Daofu, a committee member of the Russian Veterans Mutual Aid Association, for burial. The pistol and four bullets were returned to the factory owner. The deceased's belongings were handed over to the Russian Veterans Mutual Aid Association for safekeeping.

Revision of Salted Radish Transit Tax 147

The Shanghai Lawyers Association issued Notice No. 1 Tong of the 25th year stating that members who serve as legal counsel to clients must issue consultant certificates. Some members design and prepare these certificates themselves, while others purchase them from vendors. Shanghai Pinghua and Tanci Research Association: Huang Zhaolin and Others Elected as Executive Committee Members; Resolutions Stipulate Performance Methods; Men and Women are Not Allowed to Perform Together on Stage 152

The Suzhou Pinghua and Tanci industry originally had the Guangyu Society. In recent years, the number of members has grown to reach a thousand. At that time, Huang's intention in expanding the organization was to jointly operate with the Shanghai Runyu Society, inviting the society to join at the same time, so that they could cooperate in different ways, standing on the same starting point. The association's affairs are handled by a committee system, so that they are jointly responsible. However, no members of the Runyu Society attended the founding meeting, and the association still welcomes their participation. It is largely hoped that this will become a reality. The resolutions proposed and decided at the meeting with the agreement of the public were: Members performing, except for charitable obligations, disaster relief, and for the association's expenses, other performances are generally rejected; Following the central government's clear provisions, it is forbidden for men and women to perform storytelling together, in order to maintain morality; Following the instructions of the Education Bureau, the Runyu Society is welcome to join. In addition, the Guangyu Society runs the Yucai Primary School in Suzhou, which has always been maintained by the society's appropriation of funds. Tuition fees are waived for poor students, benefiting the local area and being pragmatic. Now, Committee Member Huang plans to rectify it to improve the organization, and plans to have the association raise funds to make it last longer. Mr. Huang will be hired by Wuxi next year, and the association's affairs will be temporarily presided over by the committees in Shanghai at that time. The Guangyu Society has come to this point today, and Mr. Huang's contribution is the greatest.

Professor Jackson Continues His Public Lecture at Jiaotong University: Engineering and Vocational Education in the United States 156

Professor Jackson lectured again yesterday afternoon at 4:30 PM in the engineering building of Jiaotong University. About 300 people attended. The topic was Engineering and Vocational Education in the United States. The main point was that the engineer's duty is to study theory and invent new instruments to promote the progress of material civilization. Therefore, engineering and vocational schools in the United States can be divided into three types: Apprentice schools, whose purpose is to train skilled craftsmen; Vocational schools, which are specifically for training foremen and managers. Most states have this type of school; Engineering schools, of which there are 150 in the country, with one-third affiliated with provincial universities, and the remainder funded by private donations. There are tens of thousands of students. After graduation, they engage in research, design, and senior management, and many create their own businesses. The purpose of training is to cultivate talents who invent new methods, create new industries, and promote engineering progress. In addition to basic sciences and engineering academics, the school places particular emphasis on research work, and does not neglect common sense of social sciences. After the lecture, many important issues were discussed until 7:00 PM. Professor Jackson will stay in Shanghai for a few more days before going to Beijing. This lecture tour in China was initiated by the Chinese Institute of Electrical Engineers. The travel expenses were donated by the Capital Power Plant, Qixi Yandi Power Plant, Hangzhou Electric Company, Jiaotong University, Tsinghua University, National Central University, Peiyang University, Zhejiang University, Jinling University, the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture, Zhabei Water and Electricity Company, and other organizations.

Concession Opium and Drug Cases Handled According to Opium and Drug Regulations: Director Guo Yunguan Negotiates with the Municipal Council, Agreement to Take Effect from the 11th of This Month 159

Recognizing the great harm caused by opium, the central government is determined to ban it in stages and has specially appointed Military Affairs Commission Chairman Chiang as the Director-General of Opium Suppression. At the same time, the previously promulgated Opium Suppression Law and the articles on the treatment of opium crimes in the new Criminal Code have been abolished. All opium and drug cases will be handled seriously in accordance with the opium and drug prohibition regulations promulgated by the Director-General of Opium Suppression. However, due to the agreement made when the First Special District Court of this city recovered jurisdiction over the concessions, the court still applies the articles on opium crimes in the Criminal Code to opium cases after the abolition of the Opium Suppression Law. The Opium and Drug Prohibition Regulations have not yet taken effect in the concessions. Director Guo Yunguan of the court deeply regrets this and has recently negotiated and consulted with the Municipal Council several times. Fortunately, the foreigners also understand the importance of opium prohibition and should cooperate fully to achieve the effect of banning it within the time limit. Therefore, they have agreed to Director Guo's proposal. In the future, opium and drug cases cracked in the concessions will be prosecuted in court in accordance with the Opium and Drug Prohibition Regulations. However, the provision in the regulations that opium and drug cases should be subject to military trial will not be temporarily applied in the concessions. They must be handled as ordinary criminal cases in accordance with the statutory procedures, with a three-level, three-trial system. As for the date of implementation, it is said that Director Guo has also agreed with the Municipal Council that it will be from the 11th of this month. After that, anyone residing in the Public Concession who has an opium addiction will be subject to more severe punishment once arrested.

Zheng Taihong's Beloved Wife Dies in Difficult Labor, Lawsuit Involving the Court 160

The Director of Hongkou Obstetrics Hospital is Accused of Negligence. The Plaintiff Eloquently Recounts the Doctor's Extortion of Surgical Fees.

The Hongkou Obstetrics Hospital, located at 913 Haining Road, was founded by Shen Zhaoquan from Nantong, with Shen himself serving as the director. On the night of December 1st of last year, the wife of Zheng Taici, an employee of the Ningbo Daily newspaper residing at 12 Lane 37, Beihe Road, went into labor. Two obstetricians, male and female, from the hospital were invited to the home to assist in the delivery. After the two doctors performed surgery, the fetus was extracted, already dead. The woman was ill from that point on, and although the hospital continually sent doctors to treat her, she still died on the 7th of that month. Zheng Taici was saddened by the loss of his child and mourned the death of his wife. He was convinced that it was due to the negligence of the hospital's doctors, and he filed a criminal self-prosecution with the First Special District District Court against its director, Shen Zhaoquan, for injury and fraud. Shen, however, was unwilling to accept this blame, so he also sued Zheng Taici for defamation, etc. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Yang held a court hearing, summoning both parties for investigation. According to the plaintiff Zheng Taici's statement, on the night of November 1st, he went to the Hongkou Hospital to request a doctor. The hospital immediately dispatched

a female doctor surnamed He and a male doctor surnamed Zhang to his home. They first gave the woman an injection, but she still did not give birth. The doctor then said that surgery was necessary and that the surgical fee had different grades, roughly from 70 to 300 yuan. Because of my financial difficulties, I repeatedly asked for a reduction, and the result was reduced to 35 yuan, and I was asked to sign a statement stating that I would not be responsible for the danger to life, and the surgical fee had to be paid first. I only paid four yuan at the time, and it was late at night, so there was no way to raise the remaining 31 yuan. The doctor then ordered a statement to be written, limiting the

deadline to 2:00 PM, and both documents required me to find a guarantor. I had to turn to the second landlord, surnamed Cai, to sign as a guarantor, and the doctor then performed the procedure. It was not until 3:30 that the fetus was extracted. They then said that the child's life could not be guaranteed, and they would be responsible for the woman. When they left, they asked for car fare, so I gave them two small dollars and 24 copper coins. From the deadline day on, the hospital continually sent people to ask for the remaining surgical fee, claiming that the female doctor surnamed He was going elsewhere and the procedures should be settled, and ordered me to write a report to the director, stating that the woman

was no longer in danger. On the fourth day, I went to see the director and told him about the attitude of the two doctors He and Zhang that night. The defendant then claimed that the hospital's directors were all famous people in Shanghai, and denied that the two doctors He and Zhang had extorted money. On one hand, he personally accompanied Doctor Wei to my home, prescribed two kinds of medicines, which I purchased, and gave the woman an injection. Unexpectedly, the woman died on the 7th. Even after her death, blood continued to flow. I had consulted with various doctors and only then learned that the injection given by the defendant could only

relieve pain and reduce fever, and not replenish blood or stop bleeding. Based on this, the woman was actually killed by the doctor, etc. When questioned, the defendant Shen Zhaoquan admitted that because the female doctor surnamed He was going elsewhere, the accounting department went to ask for the remaining fee. He then said that Zheng had never mentioned bleeding in the notes he wrote repeatedly. When I went to see the patient, I saw that her fever had increased to 41 degrees, and the symptoms were dangerous. I blamed him for not using a midwife first. Zheng then begged me to do my best to treat her, and I prescribed two medicines. However, Zheng only purchased one of the fever-reducing medicines, so I ordered Doctor Wei Yueyuan to give an injection. On the deadline day, Doctor Wei went again, and the woman had already entered a

comatose state. Wei did not want to continue the treatment. Zheng was immediately angry and said, "You can leave." When Zheng heard Shen's testimony, he immediately argued that he had never trusted midwives, and had not asked for a midwife this time either. As for the two medicines prescribed by the defendant at the time, I purchased them simultaneously from the Sino-American Pharmacy on Haining Road. Unexpectedly, the defendant did not know why and only used one medicine for injection, and did not use the medicine that could save lives. When he spoke, he also presented the pharmacy's invoice as proof. Judge Yang said that the case still needed to be investigated and ordered a postponement for another hearing.

Appeal Hearing on Abuse of Book Boy Opens: Judge Angrily Rebukes College Student 161

Book Boy Suddenly Sobbed When He Saw His Biological Father, Recounting the Horrific Details of Abuse Vividly.

-Judge Rebukes Appellant for Being Inhuman-

Zhong Qichang, a 23-year-old college student from Pinghu residing at 36 Baokang Lane 315, Xiafei Road, French Concession, bought Chu Along's son, Lai Fa (now 9 years old), a villager outside the South Gate of Pinghu, as a book boy two years ago. He brought him to Shanghai, making him do adult work. In the evening, he made him serve Zhong while he smoked opium, and only allowed him to sleep at 2:00 or 3:00 AM. If he was careless in his work or dozed off at night, he would be beaten with sticks. He also restricted his food intake, causing Lai Fa to be covered in

injuries and bruises, hindering his development. On the night of November 14th of last year, Zhong beat Lai Fa severely. The second landlord, Li Liansheng, a detective from the French Concession police station, discovered that the child Lai Fa had serious injuries. Considering Zhong to be inhumane, he reported it to the French Concession police station, who arrested Zhong Qichang and searched out opium smoking paraphernalia and rattan and wooden sticks used to beat the child. He was sent to the Second Special Court, where the French Concession Police Department filed a public prosecution against him for four crimes: obstructing freedom, enslaving someone, injury, and opium use. After a trial by Presiding Judge Wang Gangxu,

Zhong Qichang was sentenced on November 28th of last year to six months in prison for inflicting abuse on a man under the age of sixteen, thereby obstructing his natural physical development; one year in prison for enslaving someone; and a fine of six qian for opium use. Zhong refused to accept the verdict and appealed to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court.

The Third Branch of the High Court, based on the appeal, held a hearing yesterday by Sun Honglin, Wang Yue, and Li Changnian, three judges, together with Chief Prosecutor Zhao Shibei, in the Third Criminal Court. Judge Sun presided over the trial. Attorney Gu Shouxi appeared in court on behalf of the French Concession Police Department. The appellant Zhong Qichang arrived with his defense attorney. After questioning Zhong about his age and place of origin, he stated the reasons for his appeal, saying that he was currently studying in the Literature Department of Chi Chih University in Jiangwan, and had never committed a crime before. The claim that he had enslaved someone was simply not true. Lai Fa was taken in because his father was

very poor. Lai Fa was fostered in my home. At that time, I was studying in Shanghai, and my father took him in. The next year, the child's father came to borrow 17 yuan, and a note was written. He also presented a red paper note (which stated that the note was written by Chu Along, because his eldest son Xingguan was sick and had no money for treatment, so he asked Young Master Zhong to borrow 17 yuan, with no interest, to be repaid in five years. It was signed Chu Along on the first day of the seventh month of the lunar calendar in the 23rd year of the Republic of China). As for the injury, I did not beat him. The child was very naughty and playful, and was injured falling down the stairs.

The opium smoking paraphernalia was used by my father in the past, so it was not discarded. I sometimes had stomach problems and occasionally used it. He also stated that the child's father, Chu Along, came to Shanghai yesterday and was also in court today, requesting to be summoned, etc. Then the witness, the child Chu Lai Fa, was summoned to the front, stating he was forty-four years old, a chef from Pinghu. Lai Fa is my son. Because of poverty, I entrusted him to a tailor named Cai Wanshun to introduce him to the Zhong family. At that time, I did not take any money. I borrowed 17 yuan from Young Master because my eldest son was sick. I came to Shanghai to visit the child after learning about this incident. The rest of his words

were all to protect the appellant's words. But the child suddenly sobbed when he saw his father standing beside him. When asked why he was crying, he did not answer a word. The judge examined the forensic report, which listed in detail the injuries on the victim's body. Based on this, he questioned Zhong. Zhong flatly denied the injury, but the child said that he was beaten with the rattan on the table. The judge then angrily said to the appellant, "You are an educated person with high intelligence, how can you be so inhumane!" At this point, the court believed that the facts of the case were clear, and immediately ordered closing arguments, and then announced the adjournment, setting the sentence to be announced at 2:00 PM on the 14th. The appellant was still released on his original bail.

Shanghai County Magistrate Ye Rebuilds the Tomb of Mi Fu of the Song Dynasty 162

The tomb of Mi Fu of the Song Dynasty, located next to Helin Temple in the southern suburbs of Zhenjiang, had not been rebuilt for hundreds of years after the Ming Dynasty repair. It was extremely desolate. When Magistrate Ye Zhendong of Shanghai County served in Zhenjiang, he requested permission from the Construction Department to rebuild it. Subsequently, Liu Yongnian, Director of the Zhenjiang Construction Bureau, connected the tomb road to Xingye Road and Lin Yin Road. Magistrate Ye also used the old stone archway to inscribe the horizontal plaque "Tomb of Mi Fu, Vice Minister of Rites of the Song Dynasty," and hung a couplet: "The soil is enough for a thousand autumns, Xuanhe's literature and history, Xiangyang's brush; The forest is only a few mu, the Song Dynasty's official residence, the Mi family's mountain," to commemorate the relics of the past.

"The 264th inspection was held at the Issuance Bureau of this bank on January 4, 25th year of the Republic of China. The results of the inspection are reported as follows: (A) Total amount of banknotes issued: 179,119,453 silver dollars, including 161,455,623 silver dollar banknotes and 17,663,830 subsidiary currency banknotes. Total amount of banknote reserves: 179,119,453 silver dollars, including 118,271,453 silver dollars in cash reserve. This cash reserve includes 63,308,785.60 yuan stored in the bank's issuing general branch and various branches, and 54,962,667.40 yuan deposited with other banks. The guaranteed reserve is equivalent to 60,848,000 silver dollars. (B) Total amount of customs gold banknotes issued: 373,324.70 yuan. Total amount of customs gold banknote reserves: 373,324.70 yuan. This reserve includes 7,351 taels, 9 mace and 5 fen of standard gold, equivalent to 373,324.70 customs gold yuan at a fixed price of 50779. According to Article 22 of the Central Bank Law, the cash reserve shall be at least 60%, and the remainder shall be a guaranteed reserve of legal collateral. This is hereby reported on January 7, 25th year of the Republic of China." After the Shanghai Municipal Government's order and letters from both the Silk Fabric Industry and the Electrical Silk Weaving Factory Industry Associations to switch to the metric system, the refining industry has met several times to discuss and has already decided that from the beginning of the accounting year of the 25th year of the Republic of China, it will be permissible to use meters to calculate the length. Shanghai's Rubber Industry 174

— Compiled by the China Credit Information Service

(I) Origin and Development: The rubber industry in our country is also one of the emerging industries. It started in Guangzhou and flourished in Shanghai. Gradually, Shanghai has become the center of these factories. Therefore, when discussing the rise and fall of the rubber industry, focusing solely on Shanghai can represent the overall situation. The Guangdong Brothers Rubber Company can be considered the pioneer of this industry in the country. It was established in Henan, Guangzhou, in the sixth year of the Republic (now with three factories in Hong Kong, Guangdong, and Shanghai) and was founded by overseas Chinese who returned from Nanyang. Next was the rubber workshop of the Jiangwan Model Factory, which opened in the ninth year of the Republic. At that time, this industry did not attract much attention, and the factory was later closed due to financial difficulties. It was not until the sixteenth year of the Republic that the Yichang Rubber Factory, now Zhentai, was established. The following year, the Da Zhonghua Factory rose up with a grand scale, leading the industry today. Since then, numerous factories, no less than fifty or sixty, sprung up like bamboo shoots after rain in the following three years. After the Shenyang Incident and the Shanghai Incident, the number of newly established factories gradually decreased. Occasionally, there were relocations, mostly reorganizations and takeovers. Recently, closures and shutdowns have been frequently heard, and it seems there are hardly any new startups. Therefore, we can divide the rubber industry in Shanghai into three periods: the years after the opening of the Da Zhonghua Factory were the heyday of the rubber industry; after the Shenyang and Shanghai Incidents, the market declined, and the purchasing power of both urban and rural areas decreased simultaneously. With many businesses in the same industry, overproduction forced them to lower prices to sell. They competed against each other, and those with larger capital could still survive, while smaller ones were inevitably eliminated. Thus, one fell after another, and dangerous situations were frequently seen. This was the struggling period of the industry. Lately, the national economy has become increasingly depleted, and Japanese goods have been dumped in large quantities. Even when the prices of domestic products dropped below cost, they could not compete. As a last resort, they could only shut down or go bankrupt, which has reached the point of extreme decline.

(II) Existing Factories: According to the latest survey, the rubber factories currently operating in Shanghai include Nanhua, Da Zhongguo, Yonghe, Da Zhonghua, Jiaotong, Zhongguo Gongshang Yiji, Yisheng, Da Zhongyang, Zhentai Xinfei, Hongda, Daan, Shijie, Yiyuan, Da Zhongxingji, Dalu, Shanghai Baoye, Huaxing, Yichang, Huatong, Zhengda, Yongda, Da Shanghai, Minsheng, Chunhua Faji, Yihe, Xie Kang, Liya, Dasheng, Yongmao, etc., totaling twenty-nine factories. Those temporarily closed include Guangdong Brothers, Nanyang, Deyuan, Huashang, etc., totaling four factories. Those officially declared closed include Dayong, Dade, Italy, Dalai, Daxin, Jiangnan, etc., totaling six factories. Those still in preparation and not yet opened include Zhabei and Huanqiu, totaling two factories. Among those still operating and temporarily closed, the Da Zhonghua Rubber Factory has the largest scope, with a capital of 2 million national currency. The capital of other factories ranges from 200,000 to 300,000 yuan, with the most common being around 50,000 yuan. In terms of organizational structure, most of the earliest ones were sole proprietorships or partnerships. Later, the situation changed, and many new establishments were limited liability companies, and there were also examples of old ones changing to company organizations. This is because it is easier to concentrate talent and capital, and the investors bear less responsibility. This is a general trend in industry and commerce, not just in this industry.

(III) Raw Materials: As mentioned earlier, except for Da Zhonghua, the capital of Shanghai's rubber factories is not sufficient. Therefore, the supply of raw materials completely depends on external sources. Even for Da Zhonghua, which has the largest scope, only the main raw materials such as calcium carbonate, zinc oxide powder, and dyeing materials can be self-supplied. It is not easy to obtain even a nail or thread like foreign shoe factories without relying on external sources. However, there are many types of raw materials. Although they are obtained from outside the factory, they are not entirely imported goods. Among them, some are produced domestically, such as calcium carbonate from Shanghai Shunchang Stone Powder Factory, Zhaoxin Chemical Company, and Xingye Chemical Factory; magnesium carbonate from Ningbo Wufeng Factory and Zhenjiang Family Industry Cooperative; zinc oxide from Shanghai Dafeng Industrial Raw Materials Company; linseed oil from Shanghai Kailin Paint Company; and linings produced by various weaving factories. However, the basic raw material, rubber, organic vulcanization accelerators, and various colors of pigments still depend on foreign goods. Therefore, since the implementation of the new currency system, the products of this industry have once declared price increases, because the cost of raw materials is affected by foreign exchange, which led to this situation. Among the various foreign raw materials, rubber is mainly handled by the Horan Rubber Company and Hoshing Foreign Firm, while pigments are mainly handled by Defu and Inner Door Foreign Firms. Gasoline is mainly supplied by Mobil, Asiatic Petroleum, Texaco, and Guanghua. Other items are also supplied by Lulin Foreign Firm and Hao Hua Company, etc.

(To be continued)

Chinese Economic Society Annual Meeting Discusses Economic Issues 175

Next annual meeting to be held in Jinan; resolution to establish a Guangdong branch in Guangzhou

(Guangzhou Correspondence) The opening of the 12th annual meeting of the Chinese Economic Society in Guangdong was reported yesterday. The annual meeting was held for three consecutive days before closing. On the fourth day, attendees toured various scenic spots. On the fifth day, a banquet was held to thank local communities. By the end of the year, members had departed from Guangdong. The most important matters decided at the annual meeting were the discussion of members' papers, the location of the next annual meeting, and the organization of a Guangdong branch. It was decided that the next annual meeting would be held in Jinan, Shandong. The establishment of the Guangdong branch was also approved by the congress and entrusted to Hu Jixian, Ling Ji, Huang Yuanbin, Zheng Yanfen, Huang Yinfu, Huang Dianyuan, and other Guangdong members to be responsible for the preparations. Guangdong members have drafted the bylaws and methods for soliciting members for the branch. It is planned to start soliciting Guangdong branch members in January. The most important paper presented at this annual meeting was Liu Dajun's "Economic Control Policies that China Should Adopt in the Future." During the discussion, member Fu Zechu proposed several supplementary opinions to the paper, namely: 1. Control should increase production; otherwise, control is meaningless. 2. Control should make consumption economical. 3. Restrictions should increase prices to make them suitable. 4. Government procurement should be based on economic rationalization. The majority of the members decided that the above points were necessary additions. In addition, the papers presented in recent days include He Haoruo's "Conditions for National Defense Economic Construction," Huang Yuanbin's "China's Exchange Rate Method After Concentrating Silver Reserves," Gu Jigao's "China's New Monetary Policy and International Economic Equilibrium," Yao Qingsan's "Several Opinions on the Central Bank," Zhang Naiqi's "Economic Policy and National Liberation," Tang Qingzeng's "Observing China's Future Economic Policies from History," Dong Xiujia's "Highway Policy," Li Quanshi's "Discussion on China's Tariff Policy," Zhu Tongjiu's "Review of Land Policy and Critique of the Land Village Ownership System," Chen Changheng's "Monetary and Banking Policies that China Should Adopt in the Future," Tong Zhi's "Land Finance Policies that China Should Adopt in the Future," and Wu Kenyuan's "Lectures on the Results of Discussions at the Nanjing and Wuhan Members' Symposium." There were also more than ten other papers that could not be discussed due to the agenda. They will be published in the society's quarterly journal in the future. The annual meeting concluded at 11:00 a.m. on the 28th, without a closing ceremony. In the following two days, members attended banquets hosted by various schools and organizations, or visited factories or toured. On the 30th, at 12:00 noon, the Chinese Economic Society hosted a banquet at the city guesthouse in the name of the Chinese Economic Society to thank all sectors. National Averages for Elementary Education 178

The Ministry of Education has compiled a summary of elementary education in various provinces and cities across the country, which has been reported in previous newspapers. The following are the average numbers obtained based on the statistics of 263,432 kindergartens and elementary schools, 597,840 school grades, and the number of teachers, staff, and funding, etc., across the country: The average number of school grades per kindergarten or school across the country is two. The average number of children per school is forty-six. The average number of children per grade is twenty. The average number of teachers and staff per grade is less than one, at 0.93. The average number of children per kindergarten is forty-six. The average number of children per elementary school is forty-one. The average number of children in the primary department of each elementary school is sixty-eight. The average number of children in the senior department of each elementary school is forty-five. The total average annual expenditure per child across the country is 8 yuan, 6 jiao, and 4 fen. The average annual expenditure per kindergarten child is 16 yuan, 5 jiao, and 5 fen. The average annual expenditure per primary school child is 6 yuan, 2 jiao, and 7 fen. The average annual expenditure per child in the primary department of elementary school is 14 yuan, 2 jiao, and 3 fen. The average annual expenditure per child in the senior department of elementary school is 21 yuan, 4 jiao, and 8 fen. (However, according to the statistics of each province and city, the annual expenditure per kindergarten child is 44 yuan, 7 jiao, and 8 fen in Beiping; 34 yuan, 8 jiao, and 2 fen in Weihaiwei; 29 yuan, 7 jiao, and 9 fen in Nanjing; 28 yuan in Hubei; 25 yuan in Chahar; 22 yuan in Hebei; 21 yuan in Shandong; 19 yuan in Guangdong; 18 yuan in Shaanxi, Anhui, Guangxi, Jiangxi, and Jiangsu; 17 yuan in Henan, Qinghai, Hunan, and Shanghai; and the least is 6 yuan, 9 jiao, and 8 fen in Xikang. The annual expenditure per primary school child is the highest in Xinjiang at 27 yuan; 15 yuan in Shanghai; 14 yuan in Beiping; 13 yuan in Qingdao and Nanjing; and the least is 1 yuan, 9 jiao, and 2 fen in Yunnan. The annual expenditure per child in the primary department of elementary school is the highest in Jiangxi at 34 yuan; 29 yuan in Beiping; 27 yuan in Xinjiang; 24 yuan in Nanjing; 22 yuan in Hubei; 20 yuan in Suiyuan and Shanghai; 17 yuan in Guangdong and Hebei; 13 yuan in Shaanxi and Hunan; and the least is 3 yuan, 9 jiao, and 5 fen in Yunnan. The annual expenditure per child in the senior department of elementary school is the highest in Jiangxi at 53 yuan; 45 yuan in Qingdao; 40 yuan in Shanghai; 37 yuan in Qinghai and Chahar; 35 yuan in Beiping; 34 yuan in Nanjing; 28 yuan in Hubei and Xikang; 27 yuan in Xinjiang; 25 yuan in Henan and Shaanxi; 24 yuan in Weihaiwei; 23 yuan in Ningxia; 22 yuan in Gansu; 21 yuan in Sichuan and Shanxi; 20 yuan in Suiyuan, Guizhou, and Hebei; 19 yuan in Hunan, Shandong, Jiangsu, and Guangdong; 17 yuan in Zhejiang and Guangxi; 16 yuan in Anhui; 12 yuan in Fujian; and 5 yuan, 2 jiao, and 1 fen in Yunnan.) The average number of children taught by each teacher and staff member across the country is twenty-two. The average number of children taught by each nanny or staff member in kindergartens is twenty-one. The average number of children taught by each teacher in primary schools is twenty-three. The average number of children taught by each teacher in the primary department of elementary schools is twenty-three. The average number of children taught by each teacher in the senior department of elementary schools is seventeen. (Note) The average numbers are rounded off to the nearest whole number and the decimals are omitted.

Ministry of Education Broadcasting Program Today 181

Topic: Several Emergency Relief Methods

Lecturer: Gong Liping

Time: 6:30 p.m. to 7:00 p.m.

Frequency: 66 (Central Broadcasting Station)

Wartime Education Work Plan (5) Colleagues of the Education Research of Sun Yat-sen University

Wartime Education Work Plan (5) 182

5. Wartime Work Plan for Elementary Schools

A. Organizational System

The organizational system for wartime work in elementary schools takes the school's wartime work committee as the highest authority, with the team as the central organization and the group as the basic organization.

Groups are divided according to the nature of the work, such as fundraising groups, agricultural groups, etc., with ten people in each group. If there are several groups for one type of work, they are called "The Nth [Work Type] Group."

Students are assigned to each group according to their abilities, level, and address. Each group elects one representative.

Three or four groups form a team. Each team has a leader and a deputy leader, appointed by the principal from teachers and students.

Teachers serve as instructors for each group.

Staff and workers freely participate in the work of a certain group.

The school's wartime work committee is chaired by the principal and has the following departments: 1. Personnel Registration Department; 2. Needs Investigation Department; 3. Skills Training Department; 4. Curriculum Guidance Department; 5. Social Work Department.

Each country is both a constituent part of this team and is still under the jurisdiction of a certain part of the school committee to seek consistency in the work of the entire school.

The organizational chart for each level is shown below.

B. Work Outline

Teachers guide students to fill out a survey form of abilities and addresses.

Classify and register various wartime personnel.

Teachers go to designated areas to investigate the needs in various aspects of wartime.

Change the original teaching time of each subject, and extract ten hours per week to teach new wartime teaching materials. The allocation method of the extracted time is as follows:

Extract All

Subject: New wartime teaching materials

Civics: Wartime reports

Hygiene: Emergency common sense, defense common sense

Physical Education: Military common sense

Labor: Planting, animal husbandry

Extract One Third

Society: Current affairs discussion

Nature

Art: Planting methods, animal husbandry methods

Music

Extract One Quarter

Chinese: Writing slogans

No Time Extracted

Arithmetic

Supplement the new wartime teaching materials compiled by the Provincial Wartime Work Committee in light of local conditions.

The teaching of new wartime teaching materials is handled by the original teachers of each subject.

Transmit wartime news at any time.

In addition to general nature, the actual work should be carried out by groups with the following items as the center. Each week there are four hours of training: 1. Distributing leaflets; 2. Emergency aid; 3. Making black cloth lampshades; 4. Fundraising (unlimited time); 5. Planting and animal husbandry.

The work situation is supervised and reviewed by the principal at any time, and inspected by the local wartime work committee at regular intervals.

The funds required for wartime work training are freely donated by faculty, students, and staff.

C. Implementation Steps

The principal convenes an emergency wartime meeting to discuss preparations for wartime work.

Teachers go to the local wartime work committee for training.

Members of the school's wartime work committee take an oath.

Promote the necessity of wartime work to students and their parents.

Investigate the abilities, interests, and addresses of all school staff, students, and workers.

Announce the names of the group members.

Each group elects representatives.

The school committee investigates wartime needs and designates each team to be responsible for meeting them.

Hold team meetings to formulate a work outline.

Raise funds and purchase equipment.

Implement training.

Start work. (To be continued)

Children's Educational Novel

Little Boy (1) (4) (5) 184

— Written by Zheng Xiaocang

"I didn't! I didn't!" Niede cried, his head buried in his knees, because in the many eyes that were staring at him, he felt the suspicion and displeasure expressed there, which was really unbearable.

"I hope you didn't." Mr. Pei said, paused for a moment, as if to give the criminal, whoever he was, another chance to confess, but no one spoke, only a few children's sympathetic sighs broke the boring silence. Mr. Pei then shook his head and said regretfully:

"Then now there is no other way to think about it, I only have one sentence to say: that is, I don't want to mention this matter again, I want you all to follow my example. I certainly can't expect you to treat the person you suspect, whoever he is, as well as before this matter was discovered, but I do hope and wish you not to give the suspected person the slightest bit of suffering—he has suffered enough already. Now everyone, do your homework."

So they took out their books, while Nada said to Aimi in a low voice: "Uncle Pei is too forgiving of Niede."

"Don't be verbose." Aimi roared at him, feeling that this matter had tarnished the honor of them all.

Gold Market Supply and Demand in Balance, Hovering Around the 50 Yuan Mark, Resulting in a Slight Increase of Seven Jiao… Trading Was Very Quiet

Yesterday, the gold market initially experienced a sharp drop due to large transactions, but sellers took advantage of the high prices to sell off. The balancing tax was low, and after the rise, prices returned. Later, although there was buying activity, the upward trend was only temporary, and the overall trend remained fluctuating. In the early morning, overseas silver markets showed stability in British sugar and American prices. Brokers claimed that the selling price had fallen after large-scale sales, but the market was still stable. After the market closed, sellers dominated the listed prices. Forward silver prices in Montreux fell by 1.35 to 1.5 fen. Exchange rates rose slightly, and London raw gold decreased by half a penny, boosting confidence. Over-the-counter forward trading opened, rising to 52.3 yuan due to purchases by Fuxingyong and others. The Central Bank's listed exchange rates were announced, with British and American rates unchanged, and the customs gold unit remaining stable. The standard gold bar listing fell to 1148 yuan. Dadecheng, Fuxingyong, Shenfeng, and Lai sold, causing the price to drop to around 49 yuan. Early news indicated a slight increase, but after opening, the price dropped due to Shenfeng's continued sales. However, buying interest was strong, and the price soon rebounded to outside the 50 yuan mark, gradually rising. But large investors took advantage of the high prices to sell, and the price soon fell again. Banks were alternately buying and selling. The HSBC's listed exchange rates were announced, with British and American rates unchanged. At this point, the price fluctuated around the 50 yuan mark, remaining very stable. Later, with Shunmao supplying, the silver balancing tax was announced to have fallen by 5.5 fen, briefly dropping to 48.6 yuan. The foreign exchange market remained stable. Huixiang frequently purchased, gradually pulling the price up, rebounding to above 50 yuan. Confidence suddenly improved, and buying interest increased, leading to another price surge. However, large investors took advantage of the high prices to sell, and the trend fluctuated again at noon. The over-the-counter market remained stable after opening, with few transactions. Large investors engaged in slight activity, with supply and demand remaining in balance, fluctuating around 1 yuan. Berlin Olympic Games: Japanese Athletes Depart for Germany in Batches 197

(Tokyo Correspondent) Japan's radical advancement in sports technology this year cannot be ignored. For example, in gymnastics, at last year's student sports meet, Keio University of Tokyo independently sent a team of eight apparatus gymnasts to Europe. Even Germany, traditionally strong in gymnastics, was overwhelmed, and the Japanese team won the championship. Their intense training and technological advancements are truly astonishing. At the sports performance conference hosted by the Tokyo Youth Association last month, this reporter personally attended and witnessed athletes who would be attending the World Games performing various techniques. The mastery of their movements and the ingenuity of their routines cannot be compared to those who merely talk the talk. It is said that there are over a hundred candidates for the World Games representative team in calisthenics. They plan to concentrate them in the spring, conduct special training, and then select the final team.

The Japanese winter athlete delegation attending the Games has already departed in batches on the 21st, traveling through Siberia to Europe via Fengtian. However, fifteen ski athletes will depart on the 24th. On the afternoon of the 21st, the delegation's General Manager, Hirota, and the President of the All-Japan Ski Federation, Inada, accompanied the team to pay their respects to Prince Asaka and Prince Chichibu. The ceremony was extremely solemn.

The ice hockey representative team departed on the afternoon of the 21st. En route to Kyoto, they had a practice match against a Kyoto mixed team as a send-off. The result was a decisive victory for the representative team, with a score of fourteen to one. The crew members of the two rowing representative teams, from the Imperial University and Meiji University, held a first public practice and social gathering on Shiratori Island on the afternoon of the 21st. They also trained in the waters between Choshi and Shiratori Island on the 27th and 29th, respectively, which was their last practice of the year. Afterwards, they will go to Sahara for joint training.

Other athletes in various ball sports, track and field, swimming, and other events will all gather in Nagoya and other places in the early spring for joint training. With their excellent skills in each event, they all harbor ambitions to win medals at the upcoming Berlin Games. Our country's sports community, listen to this!
